Forceable and Non-Forceable Partitions
Enumeration with reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of property a judge may forcibly partition, state which are excluded, and explain the underlying illah for the exception.

Core Idea
A judge can force partition only of homogeneous items; utensils are excluded because craftsmanship makes them like different genera.

This passage from Al-Hidayah enumerates the categories of property where a judge can impose a compulsory partition (qismah jabriyyah) and where he cannot. Understanding this classification is crucial in Hanafi property law, as it determines when co-owners may be compelled to divide their shared property. The ruling balances the need for practical division with the prohibition of forced exchange (sarf) of non-identical items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of forceable partitions
Examine the list: mawzun (weighed), makil (measured), ma'dud mutaqarib (countable uniform), tibr (bullion of gold, silver, iron, copper), and same-species livestock (camels alone, cattle alone, sheep alone).
Each category shares homogeneity in essence and value.
2
Identify the non-forceable categories
Note the excluded items: a sheep with a camel (different species), a horse with a donkey, and all utensils (awani).
These are not homogeneous in nature or manufacture.
3
Extract the illah for utensils
The text provides a reason: لانها باختلاف الصنعة التحقت بالاجناس المختلفة (due to differences in manufacture, they are attached to different genera). This makes forced partition an exchange, which requires consent.
The illah is 'difference in manufacture' causing lack of homogeneity.
4
Apply the principle to new cases
The key principle is homogeneity. For example, if two co-owners inherit a lot of wheat (makil), the judge can force partition. If they inherit a mixed collection of handmade pottery, he cannot.
This principle can be extended via qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی کن چیزوں میں جبر ا تقسیم کر سکتا ہے اور کن میں نہیں

ويقسم كل موزون ومكيل كثير اوقليل والمعدود المتقارب وتبر الذهب والفضة وتبر الحديد والنحاس والابل بانفرادها او البقر او الغنم ولا يقسم شاة وبعيرا وبرذونل وحمارا ولا يقسم الاواني لانها باختلاف الصنعة التحقت بالاجناس المختلفة
A judge can divide by force every weighed and measured thing, much or little, and countable uniform things, and gold and silver ingots, and iron and copper ingots, and camels individually, or cattle, or sheep; and he does not divide a sheep and a camel, and a horse and a donkey, and he does not divide utensils because due to difference in manufacture they are attached to different genera.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that enumerates the types of property a judge can force partition and those he cannot. The judge can force partition of: 1) Everything that is sold by weight (mawzun) or measure (makil), whether much or little. 2) Items that are counted and similar (ma'dud mutaqarib), like eggs or oranges of similar size. 3) Gold and silver bullion (tibr). 4) Iron and copper bullion. 5) Camels, cattle, and sheep individually (i.e., when all are of the same type, e.g., all camels). The judge cannot force partition of: a) A sheep and a camel together (different species). b) A horse and a donkey. c) Utensils (awani), because the difference in manufacture (sina'ah) makes them like different genera—each piece is unique. The reasoning for utensils is explicit: they are treated as different genera due to differences in craftsmanship, so forced partition would be an exchange. The overall principle is that forced partition is allowed only when the items are homogeneous in value and nature, allowing equal division without loss or exchange.

Key Terms
موزون (mawzun): Items sold by weight (e.g., grains, metals).
مكيل (makil): Items sold by volume or measure (e.g., wheat, oil).
معدود متقارب (ma'dud mutaqarib): Countable items that are similar in value and size (e.g., eggs, pomegranates).
تبر (tibr): Bullion; raw metal (gold, silver, copper, iron) in lump form.
آنے (awani): Utensils or vessels (e.g., pots, pans).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following can a judge force partition of according to this passage?
A) A horse and a donkey together.
B) A collection of different metal utensils.
C) Gold bullion of the same purity.
D) A sheep and a camel together.

Key Takeaway
A judge may forcibly partition only items that are homogeneous in nature and value; utensils and mixed-species animals are excluded.

Forced Division of Animals and Utensils in Hanafi Law
Rulings on when a qadi can forcibly divide animals and utensils

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for compulsory division (qismah jabr) of animals and utensils and apply the criterion of gross disparity (tafawut fahish) to determine when forced division is permitted or prohibited.

Core Idea
A qadi may forcibly divide joint property only when no gross disparity exists – unity of genus reduces disparity, but difference in craft is like difference in genus.

In joint property disputes, a qadi may intervene to divide assets, but not all assets can be forced into shares. Hanafi fiqh sets clear boundaries: forced division is only permissible when the items are of the same kind and roughly equivalent in value. This lesson examines the ruling on animals and utensils, focusing on the key concept of gross disparity that blocks the qadi’s authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? Forced division by a qadi. What is the hukm? It is mubah (permissible) under specific conditions. Note that the passage does not state a wajib or haram; it defines when the qadi has authority.
2
Apply the condition of unity of genus
Based on the passage, which animals can be forcibly divided together? Camels, cows, and goats because they share unity of genus (or at least minimal disparity).
The text says 'only in camels and cows and goats' the qadi can divide.
3
Identify gross disparity
Why can't horses and donkeys be divided together? Because the disparity between them is gross (fahish). The passage explicitly states that such forced division would cause harm.
The qadi cannot force a division that results in one co-owner receiving a horse and the other a donkey.
4
Extend the principle to utensils
Even if utensils are made of the same material (e.g., both iron), difference in craftsmanship creates a disparity that is treated like difference in genus. Therefore, the qadi cannot forcibly divide them.
Craftsmanship (sina'ah) is considered akin to genus in this context.
5
Note the practical method when division is possible
When forced division is allowed, the qadi should first divide each type separately. For example, divide the horses first, then the donkeys, rather than mixing them.
This prevents disparity within each subgroup.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنہا اونٹوں میں اور گائے اور بکری میں قاضی تقسیم کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ ان کے درمیان اتحاد جنس کی وجہ سے تفاوت کم ہے۔ - بکری اور اونٹ گھوڑا اور گدھا ان کے درمیان تفاوت فاحش ہے۔ لہذا یہاں قاضی جبراً تقسیم نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ جب ایک طرف گھوڑا اور دوسری طرف گدھا جائے گا تو اس میں تفاوت فاحش کا ہونا ظاہر ہے تو اس کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ پہلے گھوڑوں کو تقسیم کر دے پھر گدھوں کو ۔ - برتنوں کے اندر بھی تفاوت فاحش ہے تو اگر چہ برتن ایک ہی چیز کے ہوں مگر چونکہ ان میں صنعت مختلف ہیں اور اختلاف صنعت اختلاف جنس کے درجہ میں ہے اور مختلف الجنس میں قاضی کو جبرا تقسیم کا حق نہیں ہے۔
Only in camels and cows and goats, the qadi can divide because among them due to unity of genus the disparity is little. Goats and camels, horse and donkey, among them the disparity is gross. Hence here the qadi cannot forcibly divide. Because when one side gets a horse and the other a donkey, it is clear that there is gross disparity. So its method is that first he should divide the horses, then the donkeys. In utensils also there is gross disparity, even if the utensils are of one thing, but since their workmanship is different, and difference in workmanship is like difference in genus, and in different genus the qadi does not have the right to forcibly divide.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage states rulings on when a qadi can divide property forcibly due to differences in value. For animals of the same genus with little variation, like camels, cows, and goats, the qadi can compel division. For those with gross disparity, like horses versus donkeys, he cannot, as it leads to injustice. The method for divisible animals is to first divide each type separately. Similarly, utensils even of the same material (e.g., all iron) may have different craftsmanship, which the Hanafi school treats as a difference akin to different genera, thus preventing forced division.

Key Terms
قسمہ (qismah): The act of dividing joint property among co-owners.
تفاوت فاحش (tafāwut fāḥish): Gross disparity in value or utility, which prevents forced division.
اتحاد جنس (ittiḥād jins): Unity of genus, meaning items are of the same kind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a qadi not forcibly divide horses and donkeys together?
A) Because they are different species and cannot be mixed
B) Because the disparity between them is gross, leading to injustice
C) Because the qadi lacks authority over animals
D) Because they are not included in joint property

Key Takeaway
The qadi’s power to divide joint property is limited: forced division is valid only when items are of the same kind and without gross disparity.

Division of Garments by a Qadi: Conditions and Permissibility
Rulings on dividing cloth items: same type allowed, single garment not, two different value not, three can be substituted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a qadi may forcibly divide garments and apply these rules to resolve a division dispute.

Core Idea
A qadi may only forcibly divide garments without cutting; unity of type or substitution avoids harm.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rules for judicial forced division of clothing and fabrics. The key principle is preventing harm (ḍarar) from cutting a garment into unusable pieces. The author (Imam al-Quduri) presents clear conditions: same-type cloth can be divided, a single garment cannot, two different-value garments cannot, but three garments allow a workaround.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
This passage governs forced division (qismah jabran) by a qadi, not consensual division. The key principle is prevention of harm, as cutting destroys the garment's utility.
The qadi acts as an impartial authority.
2
Apply the first condition: unity of type
If garments belong to one genus (jins muttaḥid), the qadi can divide them without cutting. Example: multiple yards of Herawi cloth can be apportioned without damage.
Unity of type eliminates the need for cutting.
3
Explain the single garment rule
A single garment (shirt, sherwani, pajama) cannot be forcibly divided because cutting would render it unusable for both parties. Harm (ḍarar) makes this impermissible.
Cutting is the only way to split a single piece, which causes harm.
4
Distinguish two garments of different value
When two garments have different values, forced division would require cutting to equalize, causing harm. Thus, the qadi cannot force division.
If values were equal, division might still require cutting, but the text focuses on unequal value as a specific case.
5
Recognize the exception with three garments
With three garments, the qadi can arrange a substitution without cutting: e.g., give one garment to one party and two to the other, or fractional shares. This is qismat al-baʿḍ dūna al-baʿḍ, which is permissible.
Substitution avoids harm entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہروی کپڑے کو قاضی جبر ا تقسیم کر سکتا ہے۔ ترجمہ اور قاضی تقسیم کر دے ہروی کپڑوں کو جنس کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح خراسان میں ایک شہر ہے جس کا نام ہرات ہے اس کی جانب نسبت کرتے ہوئے ہر وی بولتے ہیں الشباب الهرويه یعنی ہر دی کپڑے۔ جیسے ہمارے یہاں بولتے ہیں بنارسی ساڑھی وغیرہ۔ تو چونکہ یہاں صنف میں اتحاد ہے اسلئے یہاں قاضی جبراً تقسیم کر سکتا ہے۔ ایک ہی کرتہ ، شیر وانی ، پائجامہ کو تقسیم نہیں کر سکتا۔ ولا يقسم ثوبا واحداً لاشتمال القسمة على الضرر إذهي لا تتحقق الابالقطع ترجمہ اور قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا ایک کپڑے کو قسمت کے شامل ہونے کی وجہ سے ضرر پر اسلئے کہ قسمت متحقق نہیں ہو گی مگر کاٹنے کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح اگر ایک کپڑا ہے مثلا کر تہ ہے یاشیروانی یا پائجامہ تو اگر اس کو تقسیم کیا جائے گا تو ضرر ہوگا کیونکہ تقسیم کیلئے اس کو کاٹنا پڑے گا پھر وہ کسی کیلئے بھی انتفاع کے قابل نہ رہے گا۔ دو کپڑوں کو جبکہ ان کی قیمت مختلف ہو تو قاضی جبر ا تقسیم نہیں کر سکتا۔ ولا ثوبين اذا اختلفت قيمتهما لما بينا بخلاف ثلثة اثواب اذا جعل ثوب بثوبين او ثوب وربع ثوب بثوب وثلثة ارباع ثوب لانه قسمة البعض دون البعض وذالك جان تشریح اگر دو کپڑے ہیں اور دونوں کی قیمت مختلف ہے وہاں بھی قاضی قسمت پر جبر نہیں کر سکتا۔ مثلاً ایک کرتہ ہے اور ایک شیروانی ہے تو یہاں بھی قسمت کیلئے قطع کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی اور اس کا مضمر ہونا ظاہر ہے۔ اور اگر کپڑے تین ہیں تو وہاں جبر ا تقسیم کی جاسکتی ہے مثلاً دو کرتے ہیں جو قیمتی ہیں اور ایک شیروانی ہے تو شیروانی ایک کو اور دو کرتے ایک کومل جائیں گے تو بالکل قطع کی نوبت نہ آئے گی۔ یا ایک کر تہ اور ایک پائجامہ ہے اور ایک شیروانی ہے تو پائجامہ اور شیروانی کا چوتھائی ایک کو دے دیا اور کرتہ اور شیروانی کے تین چوتھائی دوسرے کو تو کرتے اور پائجامے میں تقسیم ہوگئی شیروانی مشترک رہی تو یہ صورت جائز ہے۔ اس کو مصنف نے کہا ہے ولانه قسمة البعض دون البعض وذالك جائز.
The qadi can forcibly divide Herawi cloth. Translation: And the qadi will divide Herawi garments due to unity of genus. Explanation: There is a city in Khorasan called Herat; attribution to it is 'Herawi' as in 'al-thiyab al-herwiyyah' meaning Herawi cloth. Like here we say 'Banarasi sari' etc. So since there is unity of type, the qadi can forcibly divide. He cannot divide a single shirt, sherwani, or pajama. And he will not divide a single garment due to division involving harm, because it cannot be realized except by cutting. Translation: And the qadi will not divide a single garment because division involves harm, since it cannot be realized except by cutting. Explanation: If there is one garment, e.g., a shirt, sherwani, or pajama, if it is divided, harm will occur because for division it must be cut, then it will remain usable for no one. And he cannot forcibly divide two garments if their values differ. And not two garments when their values differ, due to what we have explained; contrary to three garments when one garment is made for two, or one and a quarter garment for one and three quarters, because it is division of part without part, and that is permissible. Explanation: If there are two garments with different values, the qadi cannot force division. For example, one shirt and one sherwani, then for division cutting is needed and its harm is clear. If there are three garments, then forced division is possible. For example, two expensive shirts and one sherwani; then the sherwani goes to one and the two shirts to the other, so no cutting is needed. Or one shirt and one pajama and one sherwani; then the pajama and quarter sherwani go to one, and the shirt and three-quarters sherwani to the other; so the shirt and pajama are divided, and the sherwani remains shared. This is permissible. The author said: because it is division of part without part, and that is permissible.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on dividing various clothing items. The qadi may forcibly divide cloth of the same type, like Herawi cloth (a known fabric from Herat), because they are uniform. However, a single garment like a shirt or pajama cannot be cut as it would render it useless. If there are two garments of different value, forced division is also not allowed because cutting would be required. But if there are three garments, the qadi can arrange a swap without cutting, such as giving one garment to one party and two to the other, or fractional shares. This is permissible because it is a division of some parts without cutting the others, as stated by the author (Imam al-Quduri in the matn).

Key Terms
قسمة البعض دون البعض (qismat al-baʿḍ dūna al-baʿḍ): Division of some parts without dividing others, i.e., partial division where some items remain undivided.
ضرر (ḍarar): Harm or loss; here specifically the destruction of utility from cutting a garment.
جنس متحد (jins muttaḥid): Unified genus or type; items that belong to the same category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a single garment not subject to forced division according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is too small to divide
B) Because division would require cutting, which harms the garment and makes it useless
C) Because the qadi has no jurisdiction over clothes
D) Because all garments are considered indivisible

Key Takeaway
A qadi may only forcibly divide garments when cutting is avoided—either through unity of type or substitution with three items.

The Qadi's Authority to Forcibly Divide Slaves and Jewels
Intra-Hanafi dispute: forced division of slaves/jewels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on forced division of slaves and jewels, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and evaluate the qiyas used by the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Gross disparity among humans due to inner qualities prevents forced division, unlike animals.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). At stake is whether a qadi can forcibly divide jointly owned slaves (and jewels) when co-owners disagree. The disagreement turns on whether human beings, despite sharing a genus, can be treated like homogeneous goods for partition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on forced division
State Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling: the qadi cannot forcibly divide slaves or jewels. Then state the Sahibayn's ruling: the qadi can divide slaves (they are silent on jewels). Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
Both agree that voluntary division is valid; the dispute is about compulsion by the qadi.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's analogy (qiyas)
The Sahibayn analogize slaves to animals like camels and goats, and also to slaves from booty (ghanimah). Identify the illa (effective cause): unity of genus. They argue that since all humans share the same genus, division is permissible despite some disparity.
This is a qiyas jaliy based on apparent commonality.
3
Examine Imam Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Imam Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy. He argues that disparity (tafawut) among humans is gross (fahish) due to inner qualities (ma'ani batina), making them effectively like different genera. He points out that even male and female among humans are considered two genera in some legal contexts, unlike animals where they are one genus.
The key point: the illa of 'unity of genus' is negated by the counter-consideration of gross disparity.
4
Identify the mufta bihi position
After weighing both arguments, the Hanafi school relies on Imam Abu Hanifa's view. The commentary (Ashraf ul Hadaya) endorses Abu Hanifa's reasoning, noting that the Sahibayn's analogy is flawed because animals have little disparity while humans have significant disparity.
Thus, in practice, a qadi cannot forcibly divide slaves or jewels without the consent of all co-owners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و قال ابو حنيفة لا يقسم الرقيق والجواهر لتفاوتهما وقالا يقسم الرقيق لاتحاد الجنس كما في الابل والغنم ورقيق المغنم. ترجمہ اور فرمایا ابو حنیفہ نے قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا غلام کی اور جواہر کی ان دونوں کے تفاوت کی وجہ سے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا غلاموں کی تقسیم کر دے گا جنس کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ اونٹ بکری اور غنیمت کے غلاموں کے اندر۔ تشریح غلاموں کے اندر آپس میں تفاوت فاحش ہے اور ایسے ہی ہیروں میں تو قاضی ان میں جبر ا تقسیم نہیں کر سکتا۔ مگر صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ چونکہ غلاموں کی جنس متحد ہے اور اس وجہ سے تقسیم کر دی جائے گی ۔ استدلال میں صاحبین نے فرمایا ۔ جیسے اونٹ اور بکری میں تفاوت کے باوجود قسمت جائز ہے۔ ایسے ہی غنیمت میں جو غلام ملے ان کی قسمت جائز ہے تو یہاں بھی غلاموں کے اندر قسمت جائز ہوگی۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل وله ان التفاوت في الآدمى فاحش لتفاوت المعانى الباطنة فصار كالجنس المختلف بخلاف الحيوانات لان التفاوت فيها يقل عندا تحاد الجنس الاترى ان الذكور والانثى من بنى آدم جنسان ومن الحيوانات جنس واحد. ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آدمی کے اندر معانی باطنہ کے تفاوت کی وجہ سے تفاوت فاحش ہے تو یہ جنس مختلف کے مثل ہو گیا بخلاف حیوانات کے اسلئے کہ تفاوت حیوانات میں قلیل ہے اتحاد جنس کے وقت کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ مذکر و مونث بنی آدم میں سے دو جنسیں ہیں اور حیوانات میں سے جنس واحد ہے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کا غلام کو حیوانات پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں کیونکہ حیوانات میں اتحاد جنس کی صورت میں تفاوت قلیل ہے۔
And Abu Hanifa said: He (the qadi) will not divide slaves and jewels due to their disparity. And the two (Sahibayn) said: He will divide slaves due to unity of genus, as in camels and goats and slaves of booty. Translation: And Abu Hanifa said: The qadi will not divide slaves and jewels due to their disparity. And the Sahibayn said: He will divide slaves due to unity of genus, as in camels, goats, and slaves of booty. Explanation: Among slaves there is gross disparity, and similarly among jewels, so the qadi cannot forcibly divide them. But the Sahibayn said: Since the genus of slaves is unified, on that basis division will be done. In their argument, the Sahibayn said: Just as division is permissible among camels and goats despite disparity, similarly division of slaves from booty is permissible; so here too division among slaves is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: And he (Abu Hanifa) has that disparity in humans is gross due to disparity of inner meanings, so it became like different genus, unlike animals because disparity among them is little when genus is unified. Do you not see that male and female among humans are two genera, but among animals they are one genus? Translation: And Abu Hanifa's proof is that among humans, disparity is gross due to disparity of inner meanings, so it becomes like different genus, unlike animals because disparity among them is little when genus is unified. Do you not see that male and female among humans are two genera, and among animals one genus? Explanation: This is Imam Abu Hanifa's proof, the gist of which is that the Sahibayn's analogy of slaves to animals is incorrect because in animals disparity is little when genus is unified.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding whether a qadi can forcibly divide slaves and jewels. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that forced division is impermissible because the disparity among humans is gross due to their internal qualities (e.g., intelligence, skills), making them akin to different genera. In contrast, the Sahibayn argue that since all slaves share the same genus (human), they can be divided, analogizing to animals like camels and goats, where despite some disparity, division is allowed, especially in the context of booty. Ultimately, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as gross disparity prevents forced division.

Key Terms
رقيق (raqīq): Slaves; human beings in a state of servitude.
جواهر (jawāhir): Jewels, precious stones.
معانی باطنہ (maʿānī bāṭina): Inner qualities or attributes, such as character, skills, knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why can a qadi not forcibly divide slaves?
A) Because slaves are not considered property
B) Because the disparity among humans is gross due to inner qualities, making them like different genera
C) Because the qadi has no authority over slaves
D) Because slaves are too few to divide

Key Takeaway
Gross disparity due to inner qualities (maʿānī bāṭina) renders forced division of slaves and jewels impermissible in the Hanafi school, overriding unity of genus.

Division of Indivisible Property Requires Consent
Ruling on indivisible property with proof from necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the partition of baths, wells, mills, and shared walls, and apply the condition of mutual consent to similar cases.

Core Idea
Forced division of property that becomes unusable harms partners; only mutual consent overcomes this.

In this lesson, we examine a classical Hanafi ruling about partitioning certain types of property. When a bath, well, mill, or wall is shared, a judge cannot force its division because the resulting shares would lose their practical benefit, causing harm (darar). However, if all partners willingly agree to divide, the partition is valid. This principle illustrates how the school balances ownership rights with the prohibition of harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed properties
Note the specific assets mentioned: bath (حمام), well (بئر), mill (رحى), and wall between two houses. Understand that these are examples of indivisible property.
The rule extends to any property where partition destroys intended utility.
2
State the default ruling
The judge does not divide these properties without consent. The default is prohibition of forced partition.
3
Understand the reasoning (darar)
The text says 'because it involves harm on both sides, since no share remains usable in an intended manner.' Forced division causes harm, which is prohibited.
This is a rational proof (qiyas) based on the maxim 'Harm is removed' (الضرر يزال).
4
Identify the exception: consent
Mutual consent (تراضي) permits division. Partners may accept diminished utility for practical reasons.
Consent can be explicit or implied.
5
Apply to new cases
Consider other shared facilities like a narrow staircase or a shared irrigation channel. The same principle applies: judge cannot force division; only consent.
The illa is loss of intended benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يقسم حمام ولا بير ولا رحى الا ان يتراضى الشركاء وكذا الحائط بين الدارين لانه يشتمل على الضرر في الطرفين اذ لا يبقى كل نصیب منتفعا به انتفاعا مقصودا فلا يقسم القاضي بخلاف التراضي لما بينا .
He said: A bath, a well, and a mill are not divided except if the partners mutually agree, and similarly a wall between two houses, because it involves harm on both sides, since no share remains usable in a intended manner. So the judge does not divide it, unlike mutual consent, for the reason we have explained.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: assets like baths, wells, mills, and shared walls cannot be forced into division by a judge because each part becomes unusable for its intended purpose, causing harm to all partners. The judge only divides when the partners voluntarily agree, as they may accept diminished utility for their own reasons. The reasoning is rational necessity: partition would destroy the benefit intended from the asset.

Key Terms
حمام (hammām): A public bathhouse with shared facilities.
تراضي (tarāḍī): Mutual consent of all partners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a judge not force the division of a shared well without the partners' consent?
A) Because wells are not considered property for division.
B) Because each share would become unusable for its intended purpose, causing harm.
C) Because only partners themselves can decide to divide any property.
D) Because the well is considered a public utility.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a judge cannot force the partition of property that would render its shares non-functional; only mutual consent of the partners permits division.

Dividing Multiple Joint Houses: Separate vs Combined Division
Intra-Hanafi dispute on method of dividing joint houses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing joint houses and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa divides each house separately; the Sahibayn let the judge choose the more beneficial method.

When partners co-own multiple houses in the same city, how should the division be carried out? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. Abu Hanifa insists on dividing each house individually, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, allow the judge to combine shares from different houses if that leads to a more equitable outcome. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both positions and identifies which one is relied upon in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
State the exact question: When multiple houses are jointly owned, should each be divided separately (qismat fard) or can they be combined and then divided (qismat jam')?
The dispute is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah texts.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa requires separate division (fard). His proof: houses vary greatly in meaning/benefit (location, neighbours, proximity to mosque/water), making equal combination impossible.
He compares this to the ruling on cloth: if someone is appointed to buy a cloth, they cannot buy a house because the genus differs.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn allow the judge discretion: if combining is more beneficial, they can combine. Their proof: houses share the same genus in name and form (dwelling), though they differ in detailed purposes. The judge weighs these aspects.
They also extend the dispute to scattered shared lands.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, each partner receives shares in specific houses; under the Sahibayn, the judge can pool shares to give each partner an equitable portion (e.g., one partner gets a better house with less share).
This affects practical partition outcomes.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa works prefer the Sahibayn's view, giving the judge flexibility to achieve justice.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah presents both without explicit tarjih, but later jurists chose the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا كانت دور مشتركة فى مصر واحد قسم كل دار على حدتها في قول ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا ان كان الأصلح لهم قسمة بعضها في بعض قسمها وعلى هذا الخلاف الاقرحة المتفرقة المشتركة . لهما انها جنس واحد اسما وصورة نظرا الى اصل السكنى واجناس معنى نظراً إلى اختلاف المقاصد ووجوه السكنى فيفوض الترجيح الى القاضي . وله ان الاعتبار للمعنى وهو المقصود ويختلف ذالك باختلاف البلدان والمحال والجيران والقرب الى المسجد والماء اختلافاً فاحشا فلا يمكن التعديل فى القسمة ولهذا لا يجوز التوكيل بشراء دار وكذا لوتزوج على دار لا تصح التسمية كما هو الحكم فيهما فى الثوب بخلاف الدار الواحدة اذا اختلفت بيوتها لان في قسمة كل بيت على حدة ضررا فقسمت الدار قسمة واحدة.
He said: When there are shared houses in one city, he divides each house separately according to Abu Hanifa's statement, but they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If it is more beneficial for them to divide some with others, he divides accordingly. And on this difference are scattered shared lands. Their proof: they are one genus in name and form considering the principle of dwelling, and different genera in meaning considering the diversity of purposes and aspects of dwelling, so the preference is left to the judge. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof: consideration is for meaning, which is the purpose, and that differs greatly with differences of cities, localities, neighbors, proximity to mosque and water, so equality in division is impossible, and for this reason agency to purchase a house is not valid, and similarly if one marries on a house the specification (dowry) is not valid, as is the ruling in both cases for cloth, unlike a single house when its rooms differ, because dividing each room separately causes harm, so the house is divided as one unit.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on how to divide multiple joint houses in a single city. Abu Hanifa insists on dividing each house separately (fard division) because houses vary greatly in value depending on location, neighbors, access to mosque and water—factors that prevent equal apportionment if pooled. The Sahibayn argue that houses are of one genus in terms of dwelling purpose, so the judge may decide either method based on what is most beneficial, as there are both unifying and differentiating aspects. The practical consequence: Abu Hanifa’s view restricts the judge's discretion, while the Sahibayn allow flexibility. The mufta bihi position today is often the Sahibayn's view.

Key Terms
قسمة فرد (qismat fard): Dividing each property unit separately without combining assets.
قسمة جمع (qismat jam'): Combining multiple properties and then dividing the aggregated shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why are multiple joint houses in one city divided separately rather than combined?
A) Because combining them would lead to inequality due to vast differences in location and amenities.
B) Because the houses are considered different genera, so combining is invalid.
C) Because the partners always prefer separate division.
D) Because the judge has no authority to combine properties.

Key Takeaway
When dividing multiple jointly owned houses, the relied-upon Hanafi position gives the judge discretion to combine shares for equitable distribution, not requiring separate division.

Genus of House and Shop in Division vs. Ijarah
Ruling on dividing different types of property together

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing a house with a shop and explain why the same items are treated as different genera for division but as same genus for ijarah due to shubhat al-mujanasa.

Core Idea
A house and a shop are different genera for division, but treated as same genus to prevent riba in ijarah.

This lesson addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi issue: how two types of property—a house (dar) and a shop (hanut)—are categorized for legal purposes. While Quduri and Khassaf state they are different genera, requiring separate division, Imam Muhammad's ruling in al-Mabsut implies they are the same genus by prohibiting the rental of a house in exchange for a shop. Understanding the reconciliation reveals the precision of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal contexts
Note that the passage discusses two distinct situations: division (qasama) of a house with a shop, and ijarah (rental) of a house in exchange for a shop. The ruling differs between them.
Division is a forced partition; ijarah is a contract of exchange.
2
State the ruling on division
According to Quduri and Khassaf, a house and a shop are of different genera (jins). Therefore, in a division case, they must be evaluated and divided separately, not combined.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
3
State the ruling on ijarah from al-Mabsut
Imam Muhammad ruled that renting a house in exchange for a shop is impermissible (la yajuz). This suggests they are considered the same genus, because bartering same-genre items with deferment triggers riba.
Ijarah involves deferred benefits, so if they were same genus, deferment would be riba al-nasa'.
4
Reconcile the apparent contradiction
The commentator offers two solutions: (1) there are two narrations (one for division, one for ijarah), or (2) for ijarah, the prohibition is based on shubhat al-mujanasa (suspicion of homogeneity), which is treated like actual homogeneity in riba contexts.
The second solution is preferred: the items are truly different genera, but the suspicion suffices to block the contract to prevent riba.
5
Apply the principle of shubhat al-mujanasa
In Hanafi usul, suspicion (shubha) in riba matters is treated as certainty to block loopholes. Thus, even though dar and hanut are different genera, the similarity in their nature (both are immovable property yielding benefits) creates a suspicion strong enough to prohibit the ijarah.
This shows the school's caution in matters of riba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دار اور زمین یا دار اور دکان کی تقسیم کا طریقہ کار
قال وان كاتب دارا وضيعة او داراً وحانو تاقسم كل واحد منهما على حدة لاختلاف الجنس قال رضى الله عنه جعل الدار والحانوت جنسين وكذا ذكر الخصاف وقال في اجارات الاصل ان اجارة منافع الدار بالحانوت لا تجوز وهذا يدل على انهما جنس واحد فيجعل فى المسالة روايتان او تبنى حرمة الربوا هنالك على شبهة المجانسة.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اگر دار اور زمین یا دار اور دکان ہو تو قاضی ان میں سے ہر ایک کو الگ تقسیم کرے گا جنس کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے مصنف نے فرمایا قدوری نے دار اور دکان کو دو جنس قرار دیا ہے اور ایسے ہی خصاف نے ذکر کیا ہے اور محمد نے مبسوط کی کتاب الا جارہ میں کہا ہے کہ منافع دار کا اجارہ دکان کے بدلہ جائز نہیں ہے اور یہ قول اس بات پر دال ہے کہ یہ دونوں جنس واحد ہے تو مسئلہ میں دو روایتیں قرار دی جائیں گی یا وہاں ربا کی حرمت مجانست کے شبہ پر مبنی ہے۔

سوال یہاں رہا کا شبہ کیسے ہوا ؟
جواب ... جب گھر اور دکان کو جنس واحد شمار کیا جائے گا۔
تو اگر چہ یہاں تفاضل تو جائز ہوتا ہے مگر ادھار جائز نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اجارہ میں منافع ایک دم نہیں بلکہ گویا ادھار ہیں جو آہستہ آہستہ ادا ہوتے ہیں۔ اس مقام پر عنایہ نتائج الافکار اور مجمع الانہر میں سوال و جواب ہیں جس کو شوق ہو ملاحظہ فرمالے۔
Procedure for division of a house and land, or a house and shop. He said: If there is a house and a land, or a house and a shop, each of them is divided separately due to difference of genus. He (the author) said, may Allah be pleased with him: Quduri considered the house and shop as two genera, and likewise Khassaf mentioned. And Muhammad said in the book of Ijarah in al-Mabsut that renting the usufruct of a house for a shop is not permissible. This indicates that they are one genus. So there are two narrations in the matter, or the prohibition of riba there is based on the suspicion of homogeneity. Translation: Quduri said: If there is a house and land, or a house and shop, the judge will divide each separately due to difference of genus. The author said: Quduri declared the house and shop as two genera, and similarly Khassaf mentioned. And Muhammad said in Mabsut's book of Ijarah that renting the usufruct of a house for a shop is not permissible. This statement indicates that both are one genus. So either two narrations are established in the matter, or the prohibition of riba there is based on the suspicion of homogeneity. Commentary: Land and house, shop and house are of different genus, so their valuation will be separate. Their being of different genus is reported by Quduri and Khassaf. But in Mabsut, there is a case that taking a shop on rent in exchange for a house, i.e., the house is also rented and its rent is the shop, is impermissible. From this, it is understood that house and shop are of the same genus. Now there are two scenarios: either say that there are two narrations in this matter—one of unity of genus and one of difference—or say that they are indeed of different genus but there is a suspicion of homogeneity, and in the chapter of riba, suspicion is treated as reality, so the mentioned ijarah was declared impermissible due to the prohibition of riba. Question: How did the suspicion arise here? Answer: When the house and shop are considered as one genus. Then although excess is permissible here, credit is not permissible. And in ijarah, the benefits are not given at once but are like credit that are paid gradually. On this point, there are questions and answers in Inayah, Nataij al-Afkar, and Majma' al-Anhur; the interested may consult.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage addresses the division of a house with land or a house with a shop. The primary ruling, from Quduri and Khassaf, is that they are different genera and must be divided separately. However, a statement from Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut regarding the invalidity of renting a house in exchange for a shop (as a form of ijarah) creates a contradiction, as it implies they are the same genus. The commentator resolves this in two ways: either there are two narrations (one for division, one for rental), or the prohibition in rental is based on a suspicion of homogeneity (shubhat al-mujanasa) in the context of riba, where suspicion is treated as actual homogeneity. The latter explanation is preferred, as ijarah involves deferred benefits, which would trigger riba if the two items were not truly of the same genus. This shows the Hanafi use of legal reasoning (talil) to reconcile apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Genus or category of property used to determine if two items are similar for legal rulings like division and riba.
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract for hiring usufruct or services, similar to lease or rental.
ربا (riba): Usury or illegal increase in exchange transactions; prohibited in Islam.
شبهۃ المجانسۃ (shubhat al-mujanasa): Suspicion of homogeneity; a legal presumption that two items are the same genus for cautionary rulings in riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Muhammad's ruling in al-Mabsut prohibit renting a house for a shop, according to the preferred explanation?
A) Because house and shop are truly the same genus.
B) Because it involves riba due to suspicion of homogeneity and deferred benefits.
C) Because the rent is uncertain.
D) Because shops are inferior to houses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a house and a shop are different genera for division but are treated as same genus in ijarah due to shubhat al-mujanasa to prevent riba.

The Qasim's Procedure: Mapping, Measuring, and Separating Shares
Explains the qasim's preparatory steps for division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended steps a qasim should take when dividing common property and identify which steps are preferable and which are obligatory.

Core Idea
Mapping, measuring, and separating shares with road and water rights are recommended but not required for a valid division.

In the previous section, the author explained what types of property can and cannot be divided. Here, he details the procedure the qasim should follow to ensure a fair and conflict-free division. These steps are not all legally binding but are strongly recommended to eliminate future disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qasim's role
The qasim is the person appointed to divide property. The passage outlines recommended actions for him.
The qasim is distinct from a qadi; his decision is binding when accepted.
2
List the preparatory steps
The qasim should draw a map, adjust shares equally, measure the property, and value any buildings.
These steps aid memory and later valuation.
3
Understand the requirement for road and water rights
Each share must be separated with its own right of way and water right to ensure independence.
This is described as 'afdal' (preferable), not obligatory.
4
Recognize the legal status
If the qasim omits some steps, the division is still permissible (jā'iz).
Perfection is preferred, but validity does not depend on these details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
۱۵۳
فصل في كيفية القسمة
ترجمه فصل تقسیم کی کیفیت کے بیان میں ہے
كتاب القسمة
تشریح جب مصنف نے یہ بیان کر دیا کہ کن چیزوں کو تقسیم کیا جائے گا اور کن کو نہیں تو اب تقسیم کرنے کا طریق بیان فرماتے ہیں۔ بالفاظ دیگر جواز ذات و موصوف کو ثابت کرنے کے بعد اس کی کیفیت وصفت کو بیان فرماتے ہیں۔ اور کیفیت وصفت ذات کے تابع ہواکرتی ہے۔
تقسیم کا طریقہ کار
قال وينبغى للقاسم ان يصور ما يقسمه ليمكنه حفظه ويعدله يعنى يسويه على سهام القسمة ويروى يعزله اى يقطعه بالقسمة عن غيره ويذرعه ليعرف قدره ويقوم البناء لحاجته اليه فى الاخرة ويفرز كل نصيب عن الباقي بطريقه وشربه حتى لا يكون لنصيب بعضهم بنصيب البعض تعلق فتنقطع المنازعة ويتحقق معنى القسمة على التمام
ترجمہ اور قاسم کیلئے مناسب ہے کہ جس کو تقسیم کرے اس کا نقشہ بنالے تا کہ اس کی یاد داشت ممکن ہو اور اس کو قسمت کے حصوں پر برابر کرے اور مروی ہے و بعزلۂ یعنی اس کو قسمت کے ذریعہ اس کے غیر سے الگ کرلے اور اس کی پیمائش کرے تا کہ اس کی مقدار معلوم ہو جائے اور عمارت کی قیمت لگائے اس کے محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے تقویم کی جانب بعد میں اور ہر حصہ کو باقی سے الگ کر دے اس کے راستہ پر اور پانی کے ساتھ ، یہاں تک کہ ان میں سے بعض کے حصہ کا بعض کے ساتھ تعلق نہ رہے۔ پس جھگڑا ختم ہو جائے اور قسمت کے معنی پورے طور پر متفق ہو جائیں۔
تشریح یہ سب باتیں قاسم کی سہولت کیلئے ہیں کہ پہلے اس زمین کا نقشہ کاغذ پر اتارے تا کہ ذہن میں رہے اور اس کے کتنے حصہ دار ہیں اس کے اعتبار سے زمین کے حصہ برابر کرے اور اس کی پیمائش کرے تاکہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ کتنی ہے۔ اور چونکہ آخر میں قیمت کی بھی ضرورت پیش آسکتی ہے اسلئے پہلے ہی عمارت کی قیمت لگائے رکھے تا کہ جھگڑ بالکل ختم ہو جائے تو اگر ممکن ہو ہر ایک کا حصہ مع راستہ اور شرب کے الگ الگ کر دے۔
زمین کے حصے بنا کر اور ان کے نام رکھ کر پھر قرعہ اندازی کرے
ثم يلقب نصيبا بالاول والذى يليه بالثانى والثالث على هذا ثم يخرج القرعة فمن خرج اسمه أولا فله السهم الاول ومن خرج ثانيا فله السهم الثاني
ترجمہ پھر نا مزد کرے کسی حصہ کو اول کے ساتھ اور جو اس سے متصل ہو اس کو ثانی اور ثالث کے ساتھ اسی طرز پر پھر قر عہد نکالے جس کا

كتاب القسمة
۱۵۴
نام پہلے نکلے اس کیلئے پہلا حصہ ہے اور جس کا دوبارہ نکلے تو اس کیلئے دوسرا حصہ ہے۔
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
تشریح یعنی زمین کے حصے لگا کر ان کو نا مزد کرے کہ یہ پہلا حصہ ہے اور اس کے بعد والا دوسرا اور پھر تیسرا ۔
پھر قرعہ اندازی کرے تو جس کا نام پہلے نکلے اس کو پہلا حصہ دے اور جس کا دوسری مرتبہ میں نکلے اس کو دوسرا حصہ دے اور تیسرے کا بہر حال تیسرا ہے۔
تقسیم کرنے کا قاعدہ کلیہ
والاصل ان ينظر في ذالك الى اقل الانصباء حتى اذا كان الاقل ثلثا جعلها اثلاثاً وان كان سدسا جعلها ساليمكن القسمة قد شرحناه مشبعا في كفاية المنتهى بتوفيق الله تعالى
ترجمہ اور اصول کلی یہ ہے کہ اس میں حصوں میں سے سب سے مکمتر پر نظر ر کھے کہ جب اقل ثلث ہو تو گھر کو تین حصوں پر کر دے اور اگر سدس ہو تو اس کو چھ حصوں پر کر دے تا کہ قسمت ممکن ہو اور ہم نے اس کی پھر پور شرح اللہ تعالیٰ کی توفیق سے کفایتہ انتہی میں کی ہے۔ تشریح اب یہاں یہ سوال تھا کہ کتنے حصوں پر زمین تقسیم کرے؟ تو یہاں اس کا جواب دیتے ہوئے ایک قاعدہ کلیہ بیان کرتے ہیں۔ اگر شہر کا، متعدد ہوں اور ان کے حصہ برابر ہوں تو تقسیم عد دروؤس سے ہوگی وهو ظاهر، اور اگر حصوں میں تفاوت ہے تو جو حصہ سب سے چھوٹا ہے اس کو لے لو اور اتنے حصہ پر ساری زمین کو تقسیم کر دو اس سے سب کا حساب نکل جائے گا۔ مثلا تین شریک ہیں اور سب کا حصہ برابر ہے تو تین سے تقسیم کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر تین شریک ہیں اور ایک کا حصہ نصف ہے اور دوسرے کا ثلث اور تیسرے کا سدس تو زمین کے چھ حصے کئے جائیں گے۔ پھر اول کو تین اور ثانی کو دو اور ثالث کو ایک دیا جائیگا۔ اس طرح چار شریک ہیں ایک کا نصف ہے اور دوسرے کا ثلث اور دو کا بارہواں تو زمین کے بارہ حصے کئے جائیں گے ۔ آخر والے دونوں کو ایک ایک اور دوسرے کو چار اور اول کو چھ ملیں گے۔
مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے اس پر شکم سیر بحث کفایتہ انتہی میں کی ہے۔
ہر حصہ کو اس کے راستے اور شرب کے الگ کرے
وقوله في الكتاب ويفرز كل نصيب بطريقه وشربه بيان الافضل فان لم يفعل أولم يمكن جاز على ما نذكره بتفصيله ان شاء الله تعالى والقرعة لتطييب القلوب وازاحة تهمة الميل حتى لو عين لكل منهم نصيبا من غير اقتراع جاز لانه في معنى القضاء فيملك الالزام..
ترجمہ اور قدری کا قول کتاب میں ویفر زنکل نصیب بطریقہ وشربہ، افضلیت کا بیان ہے پس اگر قاضی نہ کرے یا ممکن نہ ہو تو جائز ہے جیسا کہ ہم انشاء اللہ اس کی تفصیل ذکر کریں گے اور قرعہ قلوب کی تسکین اور میلا ان کی تہمت دور کرنے کیلئے ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر قاضی بغیر قرعہ کے ہر ایک کا حصہ مقرر کر دے تو جائز ہے اسلئے کہ تقسیم قضاء کے معنی میں ہے تو قاضی لازم کر دینے کا مالک ہوگا۔
Chapter on the method of division. Translation: The chapter is about the description of the method of division. Book of Division. Explanation: When the author clarified what can and cannot be divided, he now explains the method of division. In other words, after establishing the permissibility of the essence and the described thing, he describes its quality and attribute. And the quality and attribute are subordinate to the essence. The procedure of division: He (the author) said: It is appropriate for the divider to draw a picture of what he divides so that he can preserve it, and he adjusts it, meaning he makes it equal according to the shares of division, and it is narrated that he isolates it, i.e., he separates it by division from others, and he measures it to know its extent, and he values the building due to the need for it later, and he separates each share from the rest with its road and water right, so that there is no connection of one's share with another's share, thus disputes are cut off and the meaning of division is fully realized. Translation: It is appropriate for the divider to draw a map of what he divides so that he can remember it, and he makes it equal on the shares of division, and it is narrated that he isolates it, i.e., he separates it by division from its other, and he measures it so that its amount is known, and he values the building due to the need for valuation later, and he separates each share from the rest with its road and water, so that there is no connection between some of their shares and others. Thus the dispute ends and the meaning of division is fully realized. Explanation: All these things are for the convenience of the divider: he first draws a map of the land on paper so that it remains in mind, and he makes the shares of the land equal according to the number of partners, and he measures it so that its quantity is known. And since there may be a need for valuation later, he estimates the value of the building beforehand so that the dispute is completely ended. So if possible, he separates each person's share with its road and water right. Then he makes shares of the land and names them, then draws lots. Then he labels the first share as 'first', the one next to it as 'second', and 'third' accordingly, then he draws the lot. Whoever's name comes out first gets the first share, whoever's comes out second gets the second share. Translation: Then he names one share as 'first', and the one adjacent to it as 'second' and 'third' similarly, then he draws lots. Whose name comes out first, that person gets the first share, and whose comes out again, that person gets the second share. Ashraf al-Hidayah commentary on Hidayah volume 13. Explanation: That is, after making shares of the land, he names them: this is the first share, the one after is the second, then third. Then he draws lots. So whoever's name comes out first, give him the first share; whoever's comes out second, give him the second share; and the third one gets the third. The universal principle of division: And the principle is to look at the smallest share among them. So if the smallest is a third, he makes it into thirds; if it is a sixth, he makes it into sixths so that division is possible. We have explained this fully in Kifayat al-Muntaha by the grace of Allah. Translation: The universal principle is that in this, he considers the smallest of the shares. When the smallest is a third, he divides the property into three shares; if it is a sixth, he divides it into six shares so that division is possible. And we have explained it in full detail in Kifayat al-Muntaha by the grace of Allah. Explanation: Now the question was: into how many shares should the land be divided? Here, in answering, they state a universal principle. If the partners are many and their shares are equal, then division will be by their number, which is obvious. And if there is disparity, then take the smallest share and divide the entire land into that number of shares. Then the calculations for everyone will work out. For example, three partners with equal shares, then division will be by three. If three partners, one has half, one has a third, and one has a sixth, then six shares of land will be made. Then the first gets three, the second gets two, and the third gets one. Similarly, four partners: one has half, one has a third, and two have a twelfth each. Then twelve shares of land will be made. The last two get one each, the second gets four, and the first gets six. The author says: We have fully discussed this in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Separate each share with its road and water right: And his (the author's) statement in the book: 'and he separates each share with its road and water right' is a statement of the preferable. If he does not do it or it is not possible, it is permissible, as we will mention in detail if Allah wills. And the drawing of lots is for pleasing hearts and removing suspicion of bias, even if he allocates a share for each without drawing lots, it is permissible because it is in the sense of adjudication, so he has the power to enforce. Translation: And the author's statement in the book: 'and he separates each share with its road and water right' is an explanation of the best. If he does not do it or it is not possible, it is permissible, as we will mention in detail if Allah wills. And the lot is for pleasing hearts and removing suspicion of bias, so much so that if he designates a share for each without drawing lots, it is permissible because it is in the sense of judgment, so he possesses the power of enforcement.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explains the methodical procedure a qasim (divider/apportioner) should follow when dividing common property among co-owners. The author first establishes that the qasim should draw a map or sketch of the property to help him remember its layout. He then adjusts the shares to make them equal according to the shares of division. He measures the property to know its exact size and values any buildings on it because valuation may be needed later (e.g., for compensation if shares are unequal). Crucially, he must separate each share along with its right of way (tariq) and water right (sharb) so that one partner's share does not remain dependent on another's. This complete separation prevents future disputes and realizes the full meaning of division: each owner gets independent possession. The qasim then labels each share as first, second, third, etc., and draws lots to assign them to the partners. This lot-drawing is to satisfy the hearts and remove suspicion of bias, but it is not legally required; the qasim may assign shares directly without lots because his decision is akin to a judge's ruling, which is enforceable. The passage also lays down the fundamental principle for determining the number of divisions: look at the smallest share among the co-owners. If the smallest share is one-third, divide the property into three parts; if it is one-sixth, divide into six; and so on. This ensures that the division is exact and each partner receives his precise entitlement. The commentator gives practical examples: three partners with equal shares → three shares; three partners with shares of 1/2, 1/3, and 1/6 → six shares, with the half-owner receiving three, the third-owner two, and the sixth-owner one. Similarly, for four partners with shares of 1/2, 1/3, and two 1/12 shares → twelve shares, distributed accordingly. The author notes that he has already provided a full explanation of this principle in his work Kifayat al-Muntaha. Overall, the passage teaches that while certain steps are recommended (separating each share with its road and water rights, drawing lots), they are not obligatory for validity. The essential goal is a clear division that removes connection and conflict.

Key Terms
قاسم (qāsim): The person appointed to divide property among co-owners; an official divider or arbitrator.
طريق (ṭarīq): Road or right of way; access path to a share of land.
شرب (sharb): Water right; the right to water for irrigation or drinking that is attached to a share of land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of separating each share with its road and water right?
A) It is a pillar (rukn) of division; without it the division is void
B) It is wajib, and if omitted the division is sinful but valid
C) It is sunnah/mustahabb (preferable), and the division is permissible even if not done
D) It is recommended only when the property includes water and roads

Key Takeaway
Mapping, measuring, and separating shares with road and water rights are recommended (afdal) but not obligatory for a valid division.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
8 min
The Principle of Smallest Share and the Use of Lots in Division
Explains the rule for number of divisions and the use of lots

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of using the smallest share to determine the number of divisions and state the ruling on the use of lots.

Core Idea
Divide the property into as many equal parts as the denominator of the smallest share; lots are recommended, not required.

Once the qasim has prepared the shares, the next question is: into how many parts should the property be divided? The answer lies in the smallest fractional share among the co-owners. This lesson also covers the assignment of shares through lots, which serves to satisfy hearts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the smallest share (aqall al-anṣibā')
Look at the fractional shares of all co-owners and find the one with the smallest denominator (e.g., 1/3, 1/6, 1/12).
If shares are equal, e.g., each has 1/3, the smallest is 1/3.
2
Set the total number of equal parts
Divide the property into that number of equal parts (e.g., if smallest is 1/3, make three parts; if smallest is 1/6, make six parts, etc.).
This ensures that each partner's fractional entitlement can be expressed as an integer number of parts.
3
Allocate the parts to each partner
Give each partner the number of parts equal to his fractional share multiplied by the total number of parts (e.g., if total parts=6 and partner has 1/2, give him 3 parts).
4
Understand the role of lots (qur'ah)
Lots are drawn to assign the specific shares to the partners. This is done to please hearts and remove suspicion of bias.
If the qasim assigns shares directly without lots, it is still permissible because his decision is enforceable like a judge's ruling.

ترجمه فصل تقسیم کی کیفیت کے بیان میں ہے
كتاب القسمة

مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے اس پر شکم سیر بحث کفایتہ انتہی میں کی ہے۔
ہر حصہ کو اس کے راستے اور شرب کے الگ کرے
وقوله في الكتاب ويفرز كل نصيب بطريقه وشربه بيان الافضل فان لم يفعل أولم يمكن جاز على ما نذكره بتفصيله ان شاء الله تعالى والقرعة لتطييب القلوب وازاحة تهمة الميل حتى لو عين لكل منهم نصيبا من غير اقتراع جاز لانه في معنى القضاء فيملك الالزام..
ترجمہ اور قدری کا قول کتاب میں ویفر زنکل نصیب بطریقہ وشربہ، افضلیت کا بیان ہے پس اگر قاضی نہ کرے یا ممکن نہ ہو تو جائز ہے جیسا کہ ہم انشاء اللہ اس کی تفصیل ذکر کریں گے اور قرعہ قلوب کی تسکین اور میلا ان کی تہمت دور کرنے کیلئے ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر قاضی بغیر قرعہ کے ہر ایک کا حصہ مقرر کر دے تو جائز ہے اسلئے کہ تقسیم قضاء کے معنی میں ہے تو قاضی لازم کر دینے کا مالک ہوگا۔
Chapter on the method of division. Translation: The chapter is about the description of the method of division. Book of Division. Explanation: When the author clarified what can and cannot be divided, he now explains the method of division. In other words, after establishing the permissibility of the essence and the described thing, he describes its quality and attribute. And the quality and attribute are subordinate to the essence. The procedure of division: He (the author) said: It is appropriate for the divider to draw a picture of what he divides so that he can preserve it, and he adjusts it, meaning he makes it equal according to the shares of division, and it is narrated that he isolates it, i.e., he separates it by division from others, and he measures it to know its extent, and he values the building due to the need for it later, and he separates each share from the rest with its road and water right, so that there is no connection of one's share with another's share, thus disputes are cut off and the meaning of division is fully realized. Translation: It is appropriate for the divider to draw a map of what he divides so that he can remember it, and he makes it equal on the shares of division, and it is narrated that he isolates it, i.e., he separates it by division from its other, and he measures it so that its amount is known, and he values the building due to the need for valuation later, and he separates each share from the rest with its road and water, so that there is no connection between some of their shares and others. Thus the dispute ends and the meaning of division is fully realized. Explanation: All these things are for the convenience of the divider: he first draws a map of the land on paper so that it remains in mind, and he makes the shares of the land equal according to the number of partners, and he measures it so that its quantity is known. And since there may be a need for valuation later, he estimates the value of the building beforehand so that the dispute is completely ended. So if possible, he separates each person's share with its road and water right. Then he makes shares of the land and names them, then draws lots. Then he labels the first share as 'first', the one next to it as 'second', and 'third' accordingly, then he draws the lot. Whoever's name comes out first gets the first share, whoever's comes out second gets the second share. Translation: Then he names one share as 'first', and the one adjacent to it as 'second' and 'third' similarly, then he draws lots. Whose name comes out first, that person gets the first share, and whose comes out again, that person gets the second share. Ashraf al-Hidayah commentary on Hidayah volume 13. Explanation: That is, after making shares of the land, he names them: this is the first share, the one after is the second, then third. Then he draws lots. So whoever's name comes out first, give him the first share; whoever's comes out second, give him the second share; and the third one gets the third. The universal principle of division: And the principle is to look at the smallest share among them. So if the smallest is a third, he makes it into thirds; if it is a sixth, he makes it into sixths so that division is possible. We have explained this fully in Kifayat al-Muntaha by the grace of Allah. Translation: The universal principle is that in this, he considers the smallest of the shares. When the smallest is a third, he divides the property into three shares; if it is a sixth, he divides it into six shares so that division is possible. And we have explained it in full detail in Kifayat al-Muntaha by the grace of Allah. Explanation: Now the question was: into how many shares should the land be divided? Here, in answering, they state a universal principle. If the partners are many and their shares are equal, then division will be by their number, which is obvious. And if there is disparity, then take the smallest share and divide the entire land into that number of shares. Then the calculations for everyone will work out. For example, three partners with equal shares, then division will be by three. If three partners, one has half, one has a third, and one has a sixth, then six shares of land will be made. Then the first gets three, the second gets two, and the third gets one. Similarly, four partners: one has half, one has a third, and two have a twelfth each. Then twelve shares of land will be made. The last two get one each, the second gets four, and the first gets six. The author says: We have fully discussed this in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Separate each share with its road and water right: And his (the author's) statement in the book: 'and he separates each share with its road and water right' is a statement of the preferable. If he does not do it or it is not possible, it is permissible, as we will mention in detail if Allah wills. And the drawing of lots is for pleasing hearts and removing suspicion of bias, even if he allocates a share for each without drawing lots, it is permissible because it is in the sense of adjudication, so he has the power to enforce. Translation: And the author's statement in the book: 'and he separates each share with its road and water right' is an explanation of the best. If he does not do it or it is not possible, it is permissible, as we will mention in detail if Allah wills. And the lot is for pleasing hearts and removing suspicion of bias, so much so that if he designates a share for each without drawing lots, it is permissible because it is in the sense of judgment, so he possesses the power of enforcement.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explains the methodical procedure a qasim (divider/apportioner) should follow when dividing common property among co-owners. The author first establishes that the qasim should draw a map or sketch of the property to help him remember its layout. He then adjusts the shares to make them equal according to the shares of division. He measures the property to know its exact size and values any buildings on it because valuation may be needed later (e.g., for compensation if shares are unequal). Crucially, he must separate each share along with its right of way (tariq) and water right (sharb) so that one partner's share does not remain dependent on another's. This complete separation prevents future disputes and realizes the full meaning of division: each owner gets independent possession. The qasim then labels each share as first, second, third, etc., and draws lots to assign them to the partners. This lot-drawing is to satisfy the hearts and remove suspicion of bias, but it is not legally required; the qasim may assign shares directly without lots because his decision is akin to a judge's ruling, which is enforceable. The passage also lays down the fundamental principle for determining the number of divisions: look at the smallest share among the co-owners. If the smallest share is one-third, divide the property into three parts; if it is one-sixth, divide into six; and so on. This ensures that the division is exact and each partner receives his precise entitlement. The commentator gives practical examples: three partners with equal shares → three shares; three partners with shares of 1/2, 1/3, and 1/6 → six shares, with the half-owner receiving three, the third-owner two, and the sixth-owner one. Similarly, for four partners with shares of 1/2, 1/3, and two 1/12 shares → twelve shares, distributed accordingly. The author notes that he has already provided a full explanation of this principle in his work Kifayat al-Muntaha. Overall, the passage teaches that while certain steps are recommended (separating each share with its road and water rights, drawing lots), they are not obligatory for validity. The essential goal is a clear division that removes connection and conflict.

Key Terms
أقل الأنصباء (aqall al-anṣibāʾ): The smallest share among the co-owners; the basis for determining the number of equal parts into which the property should be divided.
قرعة (qurʿah): Lot; a method of random selection to assign shares fairly among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Three partners have shares of 1/3, 1/3, and 1/3. How many parts should the property be divided into, according to the smallest share principle?
A) 3 parts
B) 6 parts
C) 9 parts
D) 12 parts

Key Takeaway
Always divide based on the smallest share's denominator; lots are recommended but not obligatory for assigning shares.

The Hanafi Principle of Partition: Dividing Based on the Smallest Share
States the qa'idah for dividing property based on the smallest share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of dividing co-owned property by identifying the smallest share among partners and calculating the number of parts.

Core Idea
Divide co-owned property into parts equal to the denominator of the smallest share.

When partners co-own property and their shares are unequal, how do you divide it fairly? The Hanafi jurists set down a general principle: look at the smallest share. Its denominator provides the number of parts into which the property must be divided, ensuring each partner receives whole parts. This lesson unpacks that rule with worked examples from the classical text.

Guided Path
1
List all fractional shares
Write down each partner's share as a fraction (e.g., 1/2, 1/3, 1/6).
Ensure all shares are expressed in lowest terms.
2
Identify the smallest share in value
Compare the fractions – the smallest numerically is the 'aqall al-ansibā' (smallest share).
If shares are equal, division is by the number of partners.
3
Verify the condition
Check that every other share is an integer multiple of the smallest share (e.g., 1/2 = 3/6, 1/3 = 2/6).
If not, the rule requires modification – see legal definition.
4
Take the denominator of the smallest share
The denominator (e.g., 6 for 1/6) becomes the base number (asl al-mas'alah) into which the property is divided.
This is the number of equal parts.
5
Assign parts proportionally
Multiply each partner's share by the base number to get the number of parts they receive.
Example: 1/2 of 6 = 3 parts; 1/3 of 6 = 2 parts; 1/6 of 6 = 1 part.

Source Text

مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے اس پر شکم سیر بحث کفایتہ انتہی میں کی ہے۔
General rule for division: The principle is to look at the smallest share; if the smallest is a third, make it into thirds; if a sixth, make it into sixths so that division is possible. We have explained this fully in Kifayat al-Muntaha with Allah's help. Translation: The general principle is to look at the smallest among the shares. When the smallest is a third, make the property into three parts; if a sixth, into six parts so that division is possible. And we have explained it fully in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Commentary: The question was into how many parts to divide the land. The answer lies in this general principle. If partners are multiple and shares equal, division is by the number of partners, obviously. If shares differ, take the smallest share and divide the entire land into that many parts, then the calculation becomes easy. For example, three partners with equal shares: divide into three. If three partners with half, third, and sixth: divide into six, give first three, second two, third one. Similarly, four partners with half, third, and two twelfths: divide into twelve, give the last two one each, the second four, the first six. The author says: We have [؟] discussed this fully in Kifayat al-Muntaha.

Commentary
This passage presents a general legal principle (qa'idah kulliyyah) for dividing co-owned property when the shares are not equal. The Hanafi jurist explains that the number of parts into which the property must be divided is determined by the smallest share among the partners. This ensures that each partner receives an integer number of parts. The text provides examples with three and four partners, calculating the necessary base number (asl al-mas'alah) using the smallest share. The author notes that he has expounded on this fully in his work Kifayat al-Muntaha. This principle is practical for judges and arbitrators in partition cases.

Key Terms
اقل الانصباء (aqall al-ansibā'): The smallest share among the partners in a co-owned property.
قاعدة كلية (qā'idah kulliyyah): A general legal principle that applies to multiple specific cases.

The Hanafi rule of partition: use the denominator of the smallest share to determine the number of parts, ensuring integer division.

Preference to Separate Shares with Pathway and Water Right
Hanafi ruling on property division: preference for separating shares with pathway and water right, and the status of lottery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating shares with pathway and water right and identify the recommended (sunnah) nature of using lottery in property division.

Core Idea
Separating shares with pathway and water is preferred but not required; lottery is recommended for satisfaction, not validity.

When co-owners divide real property, the Hanafi school recommends that each share be assigned its own access path and water right, and that lots be drawn to allocate shares. However, these are not compulsory—the judge or divider may assign shares directly without these measures, and the division remains valid. This lesson unpacks the legal ruling and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its preferred method
The act is dividing co-owned real property among partners. The preferred method, as stated by Imam al-Quduri, is to separate each share with its own pathway and water right.
This preference is expressed by the phrase 'يُفْرَزُ كُلُّ نَصِيبٍ بِطَرِيقِهِ وَشُرْبِهِ' (each share is separated with its pathway and water right).
2
Determine the legal status of the preferred method
The author explains that this is a statement of preference (afdal), not an obligation. If the judge does not do it or it is not possible, the division is still permissible (jā'iz).
Thus the ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommendation), not wajib.
3
Analyze the role of lottery (qur'ah)
Drawing lots is also recommended, not obligatory. Its purpose is to reassure hearts and remove suspicion of bias. The judge can assign shares directly without lottery because partition is a form of judgment (qadā') and the judge possesses the authority of enforcement (wilāyat al-ilzām).
The text says: 'الْقُرْعَةُ لِتَطْيِيبِ الْقُلُوبِ وَإِزَاحَةِ تُهْمَةِ الْمَيْلِ' (lottery is for pleasing hearts and removing suspicion of bias).
4
Understand the authority of the divider (qāsim)
If the divider is not the judge himself but a representative, he too acts with the judge's authority and can assign shares without lottery.
This reinforces that the division is a judicial act; the divider is the judge's deputy.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
In practice, a judge dividing land among three co-owners may choose to assign separate pathways and water rights and use lottery, but if he simply assigns portions without those measures, the division is valid and binding.
The key takeaway: the recommended actions enhance fairness but do not affect validity.

Source Text

Separate each share with its pathway and water right. And His saying in the book: 'He separates each share with its pathway and water right' is a statement of preference. If he does not do it or it is not possible, it is permissible, as we will detail inshaAllah. The lottery is for pleasing hearts and removing suspicion of bias, such that if he assigns each share without lottery, it is permissible because it is in the meaning of judgment, so he has the power of enforcement. Commentary: Imam Quduri's statement that each share should be separated with its pathway and water right is a statement of preference. Otherwise, if the judge does not do it or it is not possible, it is still permissible. And drawing lots is not necessary; it is only to reassure hearts and remove suspicion that the judge favored someone. Otherwise, if the judge assigns shares without lottery, he can do so because he has authority of enforcement, and this matter is adjudication. And if the divider (qasim) is someone else, he is the judge's representative and can also assign shares.

Commentary
This passage clarifies that when dividing real property, it is preferable (afdal) to separate each share with its own access path and water right. However, this is not obligatory; if the judge or divider does not do so, the division remains valid. The use of drawing lots (qur'ah) is also recommended but not mandatory. Its purpose is to satisfy the parties and eliminate any suspicion of bias. The judge has the authority to assign shares directly if he chooses, because partition is a form of judgment (qada). This ruling aligns with the Hanafi principle that the judge possesses the power of enforcement (wilayat al-ilzam).

Key Terms
قرعة (qur'ah): Drawing lots to allocate shares among partners in a division.
شرب (sharb): Water right or easement for irrigation accessing the share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using lottery (qur'ah) when dividing co-owned property?
A) It is obligatory (wajib) for validity
B) It is recommended (sunnah) but not required
C) It is prohibited (haram)
D) It is only for properties with buildings

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the preferred method of dividing co-owned property includes separating shares with pathways and water rights and using lottery, but these are sunnah muakkadah, not conditions of validity; the judge’s authority makes the division binding even without them.

The Prohibition of Including Cash in Division Without Consent
States ruling and rational proofs for not including cash in partition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on including cash in real property division and explain the two rational proofs (dalil aqli) given by the school.

Core Idea
Cash cannot be forced into a land division because co-ownership is in the land, not in money.

When co-owners want to divide real estate, can one owner force the others to accept cash instead of a piece of land? Imam al-Quduri answers: no, unless all consent. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning behind this rule, which protects equitable division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is including cash (dirhams/dinars) in the division of co-owned real property (land or buildings). The ruling: it is not allowed (haram) without the consent of all partners.
2
Locate the First Proof
The first proof: 'there is no co-ownership in dirhams' – cash is not co-owned property; division is a right that arises from co-ownership, so it cannot extend to cash.
This is a rational (aqli) proof based on the nature of co-ownership.
3
Locate the Second Proof
The second proof: including cash would destroy equality because one partner receives actual real estate while the other receives only a debt (the cash is owed by the first partner). The debt may not be immediately payable.
Equality (ta'dil) is a fundamental requirement in partition.
4
Note the Exceptional Case
The commentators note an exception: if division cannot be effected without including cash (e.g., the property is indivisible in kind), then cash may be forced. This is found in Majma' al-Anhur.
The exception is based on necessity (darurah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
