Default Work Allocation in Muzara'ah (Zahir al-Riwayah)
Explains default work allocation in muzara'ah before and after ripening.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default allocation of pre-ripening and post-ripening work in a muzara'ah contract according to the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
Before ripening: worker bears work; after ripening: shared equally until division.

This lesson covers the default rules in Hanafi law for who bears the work in a sharecropping (muzara'ah) contract. The key distinction is whether the crop has ripened or not, and whether division has taken place. Understanding this baseline is essential before examining conditions that may modify it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stages of work
Distinguish between work before ripening (e.g., irrigation, guarding) and after ripening (e.g., harvesting, threshing, winnowing). Also note work after division of the crop.
The contract ends at ripening for purposes of work allocation.
2
Apply the default rule for pre-ripening work
Work before the crop ripens is solely the responsibility of the worker (amil). No sharing with landowner.
This is because the worker is expected to tend the crop until it matures.
3
Apply the default rule for post-ripening work before division
Once the crop is ripe, the muzara'ah is complete; all subsequent work (harvesting, threshing, transporting, winnowing) is shared equally between worker and landowner.
Share of expenses is proportional to their share in the crop (usually 50:50).
4
Apply the default rule for work after division
After the crop is divided between the parties, each bears his own work on his share. The passage notes this is 'shared property' figuratively.
No contract remains; each owns his portion.
5
Note the application to Musaqah
The same three-stage rule applies to musaqah (contract for irrigation of trees): pre-ripening on worker, post-ripening shared, post-division on each.
Picking (jidad) is analogous to harvesting in muzara'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المزارعة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
تشریح جب کھیتی پک کر تیار ہو گئی ۔ تو مزارعت کا مقصود پورا ہو گیا لہذا مزارعت ختم ہوگئی اور جب مزارعت ختم ہو جاتی ہے تو پھر کام وخرچ دونوں پر ہوا کرتا ہے۔
لہذا کھیتی کی کٹائی کی اجرت دونوں کے ذمہ ہوگی اور پھر ان کو کھلیان میں لانا بھی دونوں کا کام ہو گا خود لائیں یا مزدور سے منگائیں۔ اور پھر گہائی کی اجرت بھی دونوں کے ذمہ ہوگی ۔ آج کل تو گانے کا رواج ختم ہو گیا بلکہ مشین سے کٹوا دیتے ہیں جس میں بھوسہ الگ اور غلہ صاف ہو کر الگ آجاتا ہے۔
بہر حال اگر غلہ صاف نہ ہو اور اس کو اڑانے کی ضرورت پیش آ جائے تو یہ بھی ان دونوں کے ذمہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر عقد میں یہ شرط کر لی جائے کہ کٹائی وغیر ہ سب کام عامل کے ذمہ ہوں گے تو یہ شرط مفسد عقد مزارعت ہے۔ عقد میں ایسی شرط لگائی جو مقتضاء عقد کے خلاف ہے اور عاقدین میں سے کسی ایک کا فائدہ تو ایسی شرط مفسد عقد ہے
واذا شرط في العقد ذالك ولا يقتضيه وفيه منفعة لاحدهما يفسد العقد كشرط الحمل والطحن على العامل وعن ابي يوسف انه يجوز اذا شرط ذالك على العامل للتعامل اعتباراً بالاستصناع وهو اختيار مشائخ بلخ قال شمس الايمة السرخسى هذا هو الاصح في ديارنا ترجمہ اور جبکہ عقد میں یہ مشروط ہو حالانکہ عقد اس کا مقتضی نہیں ہے اور اس میں ان دونوں میں سے ایک کیلئے منفعت ہے تو یہ شرط عقد کو فاسد کر دے گی جیسے لاد کر لانے کی شرط یا پینے کی شرط عامل پر اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ یہ جائز ہے جبکہ عامل پر اس کی شرط لگائی جائے تعامل کی وجہ سے استصناع پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہی مشائخ بلخ کا مختار ہے شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے فرمایا کہ ہمارے دیار میں یہی
اح ہے۔
تشریح جب عقد میں ایسی شرط لگائی جائے جو مقتضاء عقد کے خلاف ہو اور اس میں عاقدین میں سے کسی ایک کا فائدہ ہو تو ایسی شرط مفسد عقد ہوتی ہے۔
الہذا اگر یہاں یہ شرط کی گئی کہ عامل مذکور سارے کام کرے گا ( حصاد دور فاع وغیرہ) تو مزارعت فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے یہ شرط لگانا کہ غلبہ کو عامل لاد کر دوسرے کے یہاں پہنچائے گایا اس کو پیس کر رب الارض کے حوالہ کرنے گا یعنی یہ شرط بھی مفد عقد مزارعت ہے۔ یہ جو مذکور ہوا ظاہر الروایہ ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے تعامل کی وجہ سے استصناع پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اس کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اور مشائخ بلخ کا یہی مختار ہے اور شمس الائمہ سرسٹی نے اس کو اصح قرار دیا ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر فتویٰ ہے۔ ملاحظہ ہو مجمع الانہر ص ۴۸۲ ج ۲ ، سکب الانہرص ۴۲۷ ج ۲ ، شامی ص ۱۷۹ ج ۵ -
علامہ شامی نے بحوالہ خانیہ فرمایا ہے کہ یہ جب ہے جبکہ عامل پر اس کی شرط کی گئی ہو ورنہ پھر مذکورہ امور دونوں پر لازم ہوں گے اور
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۳
كتاب المزارعة
نصر بن بیچی اور محمد بن مسلم کہتے ہیں کہ شرط ہو یا نہ ہو بہر حال یہ جملہ امور پر عامل کے ذمہ ہوں گے۔ عرف کی بناء پر امام سرخسی نے اس کو
بھی حیح قرار دیا ہے۔
مسائل مذکورہ کا خلاصہ
فالحاصل ان ما كان من عمل قبل الإدراك كالسقى والحفظ فهو على العامل وما كان منه بعد الادراك قبل القسمة فهو عليهما فى ظاهر الرواية كالحصاد والدياس واشباهما على ما بيناه وما كان بعد القسمة فهو عليهما والمعاملة على قياس هذا ما كان قبل ادراك الثمر من السقى والتلقيح والحفظ فهو على العامل وما كان بعد الادراك كالجداد والحفظ فهو عليهما ولو شرط الجداد على العامل لا يجوز بالاتفاق لانه لا عرف فيه
ترجمہ پس حاصل یہ ہے کہ جو کام کھیتی پکنے سے پہلے ہو جیسے سیراب کرنا اور حفاظت کرنا وہ تو عامل کے اوپر ہے اور جو کام پکنے کے بعد ہو تقسیم سے پہلے وہ ظاہر الروایہ میں دونوں کے اوپر ہے جیسے کٹائی اور گہائی اور ان کے مشابہ اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور جو کام تقسیم کے بعد نہو وہ ان دونوں کے اوپر ہے اور مساقاة اس قیاس پر ہے جو کام پھل پکنے سے پہلے ہو یعنی سیرابی اور گا بھ دینا اور حفاظت کرنا وہ تو عامل کے اوپر ہے اور جو کام پھل پکنے کے بعد ہو جیسے پھل توڑنا اور حفاظت کرنا وہ ان دونوں پر ہے اور اگر توڑنے کی شرط عامل پر لگائی گئی ہو تو وہ بالا تفاق جائز نہیں ہے اور جو کام بٹوارہ کے بعد ہودہ ان دونوں کے اوپر ہے اسلئے کہ یہ مال مشترک ہے اور کوئی عقد نہیں ہے اور اگر کھیتی میں کٹائی کی شرط زمین والے پر لگائی گئی ہو تو وہ بالا جماع جائز نہیں ہے اس میں عرف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح جو مسائل ماقبل میں مذکور ہیں یہاں سے صاحب ہدایہ ان کا حاصل و خلاصہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ مزارعت ہو یا مساقاة ( باغات کو بٹائی پر دینا ) ان دونوں کا مشترک حکم یہ ہے کہ کھیتی اور پھلوں کے درمیان پہلے کے کام عامل کے ذمہ ہوں گے اور پکنے کے بعد اور بڑارہ کے بعد کے کام ظاہر الروایہ میں دونوں کے ذمہ ہوں گے۔
تنبیہ
اگر کٹائی کی شرط عامل کے ذمہ ہو تو مفتی بہ قول کے اعتبار سے یہ مزارعت میں جائز ہے لیکن اگر مساقاۃ میں پھل توڑنے کی شر ط عامل پر لگائی گئی ہو تو چونکہ اس میں عرف و تعامل نہیں ہے تو یہ شرط بالا تفاق جائز نہ ہوگی۔ تنبیہ - اگر مزارعت میں کٹائی کی شرط رب الارض کے اوپر لگائی گئی ہوتو بالا جماع جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا عرف نہیں ہے۔ تنبیہ - ۳ تلقیح کا بھ دینا یعنی ر کھجور کا شگوفہ مادہ کھجور میں ڈالنا۔
تنبیه - ۲۴ مصنف نے بعد القسمة مال کو مال مشترک کہا ہے حالانکہ اب اشتراک نہیں ہے؟
جواب ... باعتبار ما کان علیہ اس کو مشترک کہا ہے جو مجاز مرسل کے چومیں علاقوں میں سے ایک علاقہ ہے، قسمت کے بعد بھی پورا مجموعہ ان دونوں کا ہی ہے جیسے کسی زمین میں چند آدمیوں کا الگ الگ معین حصہ ہو پھر بھی ان کو یہ کہہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ یہ سب اس زمین میں
شریک ہیں ۔
Book of Muzara'ah. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Volume 13. Explanation: When the crop ripens, the purpose of muzara'ah is fulfilled, so the muzara'ah ends. When it ends, work and expenses are on both. So the wage for harvesting is on both; bringing it to the threshing floor is also on both, either themselves or by hiring. The wage for threshing is also on both. Nowadays winnowing is obsolete; machines separate straw and grain. If grain is not clean and needs winnowing, it is also on both. If a condition is placed in the contract that harvesting and all work is on the worker, this condition invalidates the muzara'ah. A condition that contradicts the demand of the contract and benefits one of the parties invalidates the contract. And if such a condition is placed in the contract, and it is not required by the contract, and it contains benefit for one of them, it invalidates the contract, like the condition of carrying and grinding on the worker. And from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible if that condition is made on the worker due to custom (ta'amul), by analogy with istisna', and this is the choice of the scholars of Balkh. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: This is the correct view in our regions. Translation: And when it is conditional in the contract, while the contract does not require it, and there is benefit for one of them, this condition invalidates the contract, like the condition of carrying and grinding on the worker. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is permissible when the condition is made on the worker due to custom, by analogy with istisna', and this is the choice of the scholars of Balkh. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: This is the correct view in our regions. Explanation: When a condition is placed in a contract that contradicts its demand and benefits one of the parties, it invalidates the contract. So if the condition is that the worker will do all work (harvesting, threshing, etc.), the muzara'ah becomes void. Similarly, a condition that the worker will carry the grain elsewhere or grind it and give it to the landowner also invalidates the contract. This mentioned is Zahir al-Riwayah. Imam Abu Yusuf, based on custom, by analogy with istisna', declared it permissible. The scholars of Balkh chose this, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi declared it the most correct. Fatwa is on the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf. See Majma' al-Anhur, etc. Allama Shami, citing Khaniya, said this is when the condition is made on the worker; otherwise those matters are binding on both. Nasr bin [؟] and Muhammad bin Muslim say that whether the condition is made or not, all those matters are on the worker. Based on custom, Imam Sarakhsi also declared this sound. Summary of mentioned issues: The conclusion is that what is work before ripening, like irrigation and guarding, is on the worker. What is after ripening before division, like harvesting and threshing and the like, is on both in Zahir al-Riwayah according to what we explained. What is after division is on both. And musaqah is by analogy with this: what is before fruit ripening, like irrigation, pollination, and guarding, is on the worker; what is after ripening, like picking and guarding, is on both. If picking is conditioned on the worker, it is not permissible by consensus because there is no custom in it. Translation: So the conclusion is that work before ripening like irrigation and guarding is on the worker. Work after ripening before division like harvesting and threshing and their like is on both in Zahir al-Riwayah. Work after division is on both. And musaqah is analogous: work before fruit ripening like irrigation, pollination, and guarding is on the worker; work after ripening like picking and guarding is on both. If picking is conditioned on the worker, it is not permissible by consensus because there is no custom. Explanation: The author of Hidayah summarizes that for both muzara'ah and musaqah, the ruling is that earlier work is on the worker, and after ripening and after division, work is on both in Zahir al-Riwayah. Note: If harvesting is conditioned on the worker, according to the mufta bihi view, it is permissible in muzara'ah. But if in musaqah, picking is conditioned on the worker, since there is no custom, it is not permissible by consensus. Note: If in muzara'ah harvesting is conditioned on the landowner, it is not permissible by consensus because there is no custom. Note: 3: Pollination [i.e., putting male palm spadix into female]. Note: 24: The author called property after division 'shared property' although there is no longer sharing. Answer: he called it shared due to what it was before, which is a type of figurative speech. After division, the total still belongs to both, just as several people with separate defined shares in land are still said to be partners in that land.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses the allocation of post-harvest work in a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract, and the effect of conditions that deviate from the default rules. The default rule, as per Zahir al-Riwayah, is that work before the crop ripens (irrigation, guarding) is entirely the responsibility of the worker (amil). Once the crop is ripe, the muzara'ah contract is complete; from that point onward, all work—harvesting, threshing, winnowing, transporting—is jointly borne by both the worker and the landowner (rab al-ard). If a condition is inserted that places all these post-ripening tasks solely on the worker, such a condition is generally invalid because it contradicts the inherent nature of the contract and gives a unilateral benefit to the landowner. This is the position reported in the Zahir al-Riwayah. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, allowing the condition based on widespread custom (ta'amul) and drawing an analogy with the contract of istisna' (manufacturing order). His view was adopted by the scholars of Balkh and considered the soundest by Imam Sarakhsi for his region. Consequently, the operative fatwa (mufta bihi) is on Abu Yusuf's position, meaning that in practice, such conditions are permissible in muzara'ah if customary. The passage then provides a summary extending the same principles to musaqah (contract for tree irrigation). In musaqah, pre-ripening work (irrigation, pollination, guarding) falls on the worker, and post-ripening work (picking, guarding) is shared. However, conditioning picking solely on the worker in musaqah is unanimously invalid because no custom supports it. Additional notes clarify that conditioning harvesting on the landowner is also invalid due to lack of custom. The passage concludes with a remark on the use of the term 'shared property' for post-division shares, explaining it as a figurative expression based on the property's prior state.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzāra‘ah): A contract of sharecropping where one party provides land and the other works it, with a share of the produce.
عامل (‘āmil): The worker who labors on the land in a muzāra‘ah contract.
رب الأرض (rabb al-arḍ): The landowner in a muzāra‘ah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the default rule in Zahir al-Riwayah, who bears the cost of threshing a ripe crop in a muzara'ah contract?
A) The worker alone.
B) The landowner alone.
C) Both the worker and the landowner equally.
D) It depends on who owns the threshing machine.

Key Takeaway
In muzara'ah, the default rule stages work: worker alone before ripening, both after ripening until division, and each after division.

Condition Placing All Work on Worker: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the intra-Hanafi dispute over a condition placing all post-ripening work on the worker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a condition in muzara'ah that places all post-ripening work on the worker and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A condition contrary to the contract's demand may be valid if supported by custom (ta'amul).

This lesson dives into the legal debate within the Hanafi school about a specific condition in sharecropping: can the landowner stipulate that the worker must do all the harvesting, threshing, and related work at his own expense? The Zahir al-Riwayah view says such a condition invalidates the contract, but Imam Abu Yusuf, relying on widespread custom and analogy with istisna', permits it. The later school has adopted Abu Yusuf's position as the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its effect under Zahir al-Riwayah
The condition that the worker will do all post-ripening work (harvesting, threshing, etc.) contradicts the inherent demand (muqtada) of the contract, which is that such work is shared. It also gives a unilateral benefit to the landowner. Therefore, in Zahir al-Riwayah, this condition makes the contract void (fasid).
The analogy given is with conditions like carrying and grinding on the worker.
2
Understand the opposing view of Imam Abu Yusuf
Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the condition is valid because of widespread custom (ta'amul). People commonly agree to such terms. He draws an analogy with the contract of istisna' (manufacturing order), where custom allows conditions that are not explicitly required.
Custom (ta'amul) is a recognized source in Hanafi law.
3
Trace the adoption by later scholars
The scholars of Balkh chose Abu Yusuf's view. Imam Sarakhsi declared it the 'asahh' (most correct) for his region. The text states that fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's saying.
This shift from Zahir al-Riwayah to a nawadir transmission is a key feature of Hanafi tarjih.
4
Apply the ruling to different scenarios
In muzara'ah, if the condition is placed on the worker, the mufta bihi view allows it. In musaqah, however, conditioning picking on the worker is invalid by consensus because no custom exists. Similarly, conditioning on the landowner is invalid due to lack of custom.
Custom varies by contract type and region.
5
Distinguish the extreme view of some scholars
Nasr bin [؟] and Muhammad bin Muslim hold that regardless of condition, all post-ripening work is on the worker by custom. Imam Sarakhsi also considered this sound.
This goes even beyond Abu Yusuf by removing the need for an explicit condition.

لہذا کھیتی کی کٹائی کی اجرت دونوں کے ذمہ ہوگی اور پھر ان کو کھلیان میں لانا بھی دونوں کا کام ہو گا خود لائیں یا مزدور سے منگائیں۔ اور پھر گہائی کی اجرت بھی دونوں کے ذمہ ہوگی ۔ آج کل تو گانے کا رواج ختم ہو گیا بلکہ مشین سے کٹوا دیتے ہیں جس میں بھوسہ الگ اور غلہ صاف ہو کر الگ آجاتا ہے۔
بہر حال اگر غلہ صاف نہ ہو اور اس کو اڑانے کی ضرورت پیش آ جائے تو یہ بھی ان دونوں کے ذمہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر عقد میں یہ شرط کر لی جائے کہ کٹائی وغیر ہ سب کام عامل کے ذمہ ہوں گے تو یہ شرط مفسد عقد مزارعت ہے۔ عقد میں ایسی شرط لگائی جو مقتضاء عقد کے خلاف ہے اور عاقدین میں سے کسی ایک کا فائدہ تو ایسی شرط مفسد عقد ہے
واذا شرط في العقد ذالك ولا يقتضيه وفيه منفعة لاحدهما يفسد العقد كشرط الحمل والطحن على العامل وعن ابي يوسف انه يجوز اذا شرط ذالك على العامل للتعامل اعتباراً بالاستصناع وهو اختيار مشائخ بلخ قال شمس الايمة السرخسى هذا هو الاصح في ديارنا ترجمہ اور جبکہ عقد میں یہ مشروط ہو حالانکہ عقد اس کا مقتضی نہیں ہے اور اس میں ان دونوں میں سے ایک کیلئے منفعت ہے تو یہ شرط عقد کو فاسد کر دے گی جیسے لاد کر لانے کی شرط یا پینے کی شرط عامل پر اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ یہ جائز ہے جبکہ عامل پر اس کی شرط لگائی جائے تعامل کی وجہ سے استصناع پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہی مشائخ بلخ کا مختار ہے شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے فرمایا کہ ہمارے دیار میں یہی
اح ہے۔
تشریح جب عقد میں ایسی شرط لگائی جائے جو مقتضاء عقد کے خلاف ہو اور اس میں عاقدین میں سے کسی ایک کا فائدہ ہو تو ایسی شرط مفسد عقد ہوتی ہے۔
الہذا اگر یہاں یہ شرط کی گئی کہ عامل مذکور سارے کام کرے گا ( حصاد دور فاع وغیرہ) تو مزارعت فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے یہ شرط لگانا کہ غلبہ کو عامل لاد کر دوسرے کے یہاں پہنچائے گایا اس کو پیس کر رب الارض کے حوالہ کرنے گا یعنی یہ شرط بھی مفد عقد مزارعت ہے۔ یہ جو مذکور ہوا ظاہر الروایہ ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے تعامل کی وجہ سے استصناع پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اس کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اور مشائخ بلخ کا یہی مختار ہے اور شمس الائمہ سرسٹی نے اس کو اصح قرار دیا ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول پر فتویٰ ہے۔ ملاحظہ ہو مجمع الانہر ص ۴۸۲ ج ۲ ، سکب الانہرص ۴۲۷ ج ۲ ، شامی ص ۱۷۹ ج ۵ -
علامہ شامی نے بحوالہ خانیہ فرمایا ہے کہ یہ جب ہے جبکہ عامل پر اس کی شرط کی گئی ہو ورنہ پھر مذکورہ امور دونوں پر لازم ہوں گے اور
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۳

مسائل مذکورہ کا خلاصہ
فالحاصل ان ما كان من عمل قبل الإدراك كالسقى والحفظ فهو على العامل وما كان منه بعد الادراك قبل القسمة فهو عليهما فى ظاهر الرواية كالحصاد والدياس واشباهما على ما بيناه وما كان بعد القسمة فهو عليهما والمعاملة على قياس هذا ما كان قبل ادراك الثمر من السقى والتلقيح والحفظ فهو على العامل وما كان بعد الادراك كالجداد والحفظ فهو عليهما ولو شرط الجداد على العامل لا يجوز بالاتفاق لانه لا عرف فيه
ترجمہ پس حاصل یہ ہے کہ جو کام کھیتی پکنے سے پہلے ہو جیسے سیراب کرنا اور حفاظت کرنا وہ تو عامل کے اوپر ہے اور جو کام پکنے کے بعد ہو تقسیم سے پہلے وہ ظاہر الروایہ میں دونوں کے اوپر ہے جیسے کٹائی اور گہائی اور ان کے مشابہ اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور جو کام تقسیم کے بعد نہو وہ ان دونوں کے اوپر ہے اور مساقاة اس قیاس پر ہے جو کام پھل پکنے سے پہلے ہو یعنی سیرابی اور گا بھ دینا اور حفاظت کرنا وہ تو عامل کے اوپر ہے اور جو کام پھل پکنے کے بعد ہو جیسے پھل توڑنا اور حفاظت کرنا وہ ان دونوں پر ہے اور اگر توڑنے کی شرط عامل پر لگائی گئی ہو تو وہ بالا تفاق جائز نہیں ہے اور جو کام بٹوارہ کے بعد ہودہ ان دونوں کے اوپر ہے اسلئے کہ یہ مال مشترک ہے اور کوئی عقد نہیں ہے اور اگر کھیتی میں کٹائی کی شرط زمین والے پر لگائی گئی ہو تو وہ بالا جماع جائز نہیں ہے اس میں عرف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح جو مسائل ماقبل میں مذکور ہیں یہاں سے صاحب ہدایہ ان کا حاصل و خلاصہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ مزارعت ہو یا مساقاة ( باغات کو بٹائی پر دینا ) ان دونوں کا مشترک حکم یہ ہے کہ کھیتی اور پھلوں کے درمیان پہلے کے کام عامل کے ذمہ ہوں گے اور پکنے کے بعد اور بڑارہ کے بعد کے کام ظاہر الروایہ میں دونوں کے ذمہ ہوں گے۔
تنبیہ
اگر کٹائی کی شرط عامل کے ذمہ ہو تو مفتی بہ قول کے اعتبار سے یہ مزارعت میں جائز ہے لیکن اگر مساقاۃ میں پھل توڑنے کی شر ط عامل پر لگائی گئی ہو تو چونکہ اس میں عرف و تعامل نہیں ہے تو یہ شرط بالا تفاق جائز نہ ہوگی۔ تنبیہ - اگر مزارعت میں کٹائی کی شرط رب الارض کے اوپر لگائی گئی ہوتو بالا جماع جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا عرف نہیں ہے۔ تنبیہ - ۳ تلقیح کا بھ دینا یعنی ر کھجور کا شگوفہ مادہ کھجور میں ڈالنا۔
تنبیه - ۲۴ مصنف نے بعد القسمة مال کو مال مشترک کہا ہے حالانکہ اب اشتراک نہیں ہے؟
جواب ... باعتبار ما کان علیہ اس کو مشترک کہا ہے جو مجاز مرسل کے چومیں علاقوں میں سے ایک علاقہ ہے، قسمت کے بعد بھی پورا مجموعہ ان دونوں کا ہی ہے جیسے کسی زمین میں چند آدمیوں کا الگ الگ معین حصہ ہو پھر بھی ان کو یہ کہہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ یہ سب اس زمین میں
شریک ہیں ۔
Book of Muzara'ah. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Volume 13. Explanation: When the crop ripens, the purpose of muzara'ah is fulfilled, so the muzara'ah ends. When it ends, work and expenses are on both. So the wage for harvesting is on both; bringing it to the threshing floor is also on both, either themselves or by hiring. The wage for threshing is also on both. Nowadays winnowing is obsolete; machines separate straw and grain. If grain is not clean and needs winnowing, it is also on both. If a condition is placed in the contract that harvesting and all work is on the worker, this condition invalidates the muzara'ah. A condition that contradicts the demand of the contract and benefits one of the parties invalidates the contract. And if such a condition is placed in the contract, and it is not required by the contract, and it contains benefit for one of them, it invalidates the contract, like the condition of carrying and grinding on the worker. And from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible if that condition is made on the worker due to custom (ta'amul), by analogy with istisna', and this is the choice of the scholars of Balkh. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: This is the correct view in our regions. Translation: And when it is conditional in the contract, while the contract does not require it, and there is benefit for one of them, this condition invalidates the contract, like the condition of carrying and grinding on the worker. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is permissible when the condition is made on the worker due to custom, by analogy with istisna', and this is the choice of the scholars of Balkh. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: This is the correct view in our regions. Explanation: When a condition is placed in a contract that contradicts its demand and benefits one of the parties, it invalidates the contract. So if the condition is that the worker will do all work (harvesting, threshing, etc.), the muzara'ah becomes void. Similarly, a condition that the worker will carry the grain elsewhere or grind it and give it to the landowner also invalidates the contract. This mentioned is Zahir al-Riwayah. Imam Abu Yusuf, based on custom, by analogy with istisna', declared it permissible. The scholars of Balkh chose this, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi declared it the most correct. Fatwa is on the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf. See Majma' al-Anhur, etc. Allama Shami, citing Khaniya, said this is when the condition is made on the worker; otherwise those matters are binding on both. Nasr bin [؟] and Muhammad bin Muslim say that whether the condition is made or not, all those matters are on the worker. Based on custom, Imam Sarakhsi also declared this sound. Summary of mentioned issues: The conclusion is that what is work before ripening, like irrigation and guarding, is on the worker. What is after ripening before division, like harvesting and threshing and the like, is on both in Zahir al-Riwayah according to what we explained. What is after division is on both. And musaqah is by analogy with this: what is before fruit ripening, like irrigation, pollination, and guarding, is on the worker; what is after ripening, like picking and guarding, is on both. If picking is conditioned on the worker, it is not permissible by consensus because there is no custom in it. Translation: So the conclusion is that work before ripening like irrigation and guarding is on the worker. Work after ripening before division like harvesting and threshing and their like is on both in Zahir al-Riwayah. Work after division is on both. And musaqah is analogous: work before fruit ripening like irrigation, pollination, and guarding is on the worker; work after ripening like picking and guarding is on both. If picking is conditioned on the worker, it is not permissible by consensus because there is no custom. Explanation: The author of Hidayah summarizes that for both muzara'ah and musaqah, the ruling is that earlier work is on the worker, and after ripening and after division, work is on both in Zahir al-Riwayah. Note: If harvesting is conditioned on the worker, according to the mufta bihi view, it is permissible in muzara'ah. But if in musaqah, picking is conditioned on the worker, since there is no custom, it is not permissible by consensus. Note: If in muzara'ah harvesting is conditioned on the landowner, it is not permissible by consensus because there is no custom. Note: 3: Pollination [i.e., putting male palm spadix into female]. Note: 24: The author called property after division 'shared property' although there is no longer sharing. Answer: he called it shared due to what it was before, which is a type of figurative speech. After division, the total still belongs to both, just as several people with separate defined shares in land are still said to be partners in that land.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses the allocation of post-harvest work in a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract, and the effect of conditions that deviate from the default rules. The default rule, as per Zahir al-Riwayah, is that work before the crop ripens (irrigation, guarding) is entirely the responsibility of the worker (amil). Once the crop is ripe, the muzara'ah contract is complete; from that point onward, all work—harvesting, threshing, winnowing, transporting—is jointly borne by both the worker and the landowner (rab al-ard). If a condition is inserted that places all these post-ripening tasks solely on the worker, such a condition is generally invalid because it contradicts the inherent nature of the contract and gives a unilateral benefit to the landowner. This is the position reported in the Zahir al-Riwayah. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, allowing the condition based on widespread custom (ta'amul) and drawing an analogy with the contract of istisna' (manufacturing order). His view was adopted by the scholars of Balkh and considered the soundest by Imam Sarakhsi for his region. Consequently, the operative fatwa (mufta bihi) is on Abu Yusuf's position, meaning that in practice, such conditions are permissible in muzara'ah if customary. The passage then provides a summary extending the same principles to musaqah (contract for tree irrigation). In musaqah, pre-ripening work (irrigation, pollination, guarding) falls on the worker, and post-ripening work (picking, guarding) is shared. However, conditioning picking solely on the worker in musaqah is unanimously invalid because no custom supports it. Additional notes clarify that conditioning harvesting on the landowner is also invalid due to lack of custom. The passage concludes with a remark on the use of the term 'shared property' for post-division shares, explaining it as a figurative expression based on the property's prior state.

Key Terms
تعامل (ta‘āmul): Widespread customary practice among people; used as a basis for legal permissibility.
ظاہر الروایہ (ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The well-known and authoritative transmissions from the three founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) compiled by Imam Muhammad.
استصناع (istiṣnā‘): A contract of manufacturing or ordering goods, where custom allows flexible terms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if the landowner conditions that the worker must do all harvesting and threshing in a muzara'ah contract?
A) The contract becomes void (fasid) because the condition is invalid.
B) The condition is valid and the contract remains sound because of customary practice.
C) The contract is valid but the condition is void and unenforceable.
D) The worker is not bound by the condition and may abandon the work.

Key Takeaway
A condition placing post-ripening work solely on the worker in muzara'ah is permissible according to the operative Hanafi fatwa, due to custom, even though the default ruling holds that such work is shared.

Musaqat: Valid vs. Fasid Contracts Based on Known Termination Period
Distinguishing valid from fasid musaqat based on knowledge of termination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and fasid musaqat contracts based on whether the termination period is known (ma'lum) or unknown (majhul), and state the Hanafi ruling in each case.

Core Idea
In musaqat, a known end (e.g., first harvest) validates the contract; an uncertain end (e.g., when roots dry) renders it fasid.

This lesson examines a key condition for the validity of a musaqat (sharecropping) contract: the termination period must be known. The Hanafi school rules that if the period is unspecified or tied to an uncertain event, the contract is fasid (voidable), entitling the worker only to an equivalent wage. We will explore the distinction through examples of clover, date palms, and other plants, and trace the proof from the authoritative texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Contrast the first scenario (work until first harvest, term known) with the second (work until roots dry, term unknown). Note the different rulings: valid vs. fasid.
The critical factor is knowledge of the termination point.
2
Extract the ratio legis (illah)
Why does an unknown period invalidate the contract? Because it introduces gharar (uncertainty) into the partnership; the parties cannot know when obligations end.
Gharar in the term is a recognized cause of fasid in Hanafi muamalat.
3
Analyze the proof from Badai' al-Sanai'
The quote from Badai' explicitly states: if the time of cutting (jazzah) is known, the contract is valid; if not, it is fasid. This applies to both fresh plants and fruit trees by analogy.
The proof is qiyas: comparing the unknown termination to the known case of fruit trees.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on scope
Some late commentators (e.g. author of 'Inayah) argued that the proof only applies to fresh roots (ratbah), not to palm trees (nakheel). But the majority (including the text of Badai') includes both.
The relied-upon position is that all plants are subject to the same condition of known term.
5
Apply to a concrete case
Given a scenario: owner hands over a field of clover to a worker with the instruction 'tend until the last harvest' (a known annual event) – the contract is valid. If he says 'tend until the roots dry' (no known time) – the contract is fasid.
The worker in the fasid case still deserves ujrat al-mithl for work performed.

اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ جائے گی تو مدت مجہول ہوگئی ۔ ۲۲۱ كتاب المساقات تشریح پہلے مسئلہ میں برسیم کی جڑ میں جنس سے مراد آخری لو ہے دینے کو بیان مدت کے بغیر جائز کہا ہے اور اس کو فاسد کہ رہے ہیں ۔ تو فرق یہ ہے کہ پہلے پیج کے حاصل ہونے تک دیا تھا اور اس کا وقت معلوم ہے۔ اور یہاں مراد یہ ہے کہ جب تک حفاظت کرے کہ اس کی جڑوں کی اگان ختم ہو جائے بلکہ جڑیں خشک ہو جائے تو خشک ہونے کی اور اگان کی مدت معلوم نہیں بلکہ زمین میں وہ جب تک رہے گی اگان جاری رہے گا اور سوکھنا متحقق نہ ہو گا تو مدت مجہول ہے اسلئے بغیر بیان مدت کے یہ معاملہ جائز نہ ہوگا یا اس سے اگان ختم ہونے گی اور سوکھنے کی شرط نہیں لگائی بلکہ مطلقاً آخری لو دے دی تو بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ عقد فاسد ہے۔ مگر یہ دلیل جو بیان کی گئی ہے صرف اصول رطبہ میں جاری ہو سکتی ہے بخیل میں نہیں اس وجہ سے بعض شراح نے کہا ہے کہ مصنف نے تخیل کی دلیل بیان نہیں فرمائی جیسا کہ صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا ہے۔ مذکورہ دلیل دونوں کی ہو سکتی ہے اور مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ کھجور کا درخت دے دیا اور کہا کہ اسکی حفاظت کرو اور یہ عقد ہمارے اور تمہارے درمیان جب تک رہے گا جب تک کہ یہ کھجور سوکھ نہ جائے تو یہ عقد فاسد ہے اسلئے کہ اس کی مدت مجہول ہے البتہ اگر خیل میں مطلقا کہا اور سو کھنے وغیرہ کی شرط انہیں لگائی تو عقد صحیح ہوگا اور حسب سابق پہلے پھلوں پر یہ عقد واقع ہو گا مگر برسیم ولہسن کے اندر اطلاق کی صورت میں بھی فساد ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں نہایت معلومہ نہیں ہے۔ تنبیہ ۔ پہلی اور دوسری صورت میں فرق کا مدار نہایت کے علم وعدم علم پر ہے وہاں نہایت معلوم ہے تو اس کو جائز کہا ہے اور یہاں نہایت معلوم نہیں اسلئے اس کو فاسد کہا لہذا اگر اس نے کھجور کے درخت یا برسیم عامل کے حوالہ کی اور اسے حتى تذهب اصولها کی شرط نہیں لگائی اور پھل کے آنے اور بیچ کے آنے کا وقت معلوم ہے تو یہ عقد جائز ہے اور اگر بیچ کے آنے کا وقت معلوم نہ ہو تو پھر عقد فاسد ہوگا۔ شامی ص ۱۸۳ ج ۵۔ مگر انہوں نے پہلی لو آنے پر عقد کو واقع کیا ہے نیز ملاحظہ ہو مجمع الا نہر ص ۴۸۶ ج ۲ ۔ تنبیہ - علامہ کا سائی فرماتے ہیں ولو دفع ارضاً ليزرع فيها الرطاب او دفع ارضا فيها اصول رطبة ثابتة و لم يسم المدة فان كان شيئاً ليس لابتداء نباته ولا لانتهاء جذه وقت معلوم فالمعاملة فاسدة وان كان وقت جذه معلوماً يجوز و يقع على الجذةِ الاولى كما في الشجرة المثمرة - (بدائع ص ١٨٦ ج ٢) یہ عبارت بالکل صاف ہے کہ جواز و عدم جواز کامدار نہایت کے علم وعدم علم پر ہے خلاصہ کلام صاحب ہدایہ کا کلام صاف نہیں بلکہ کلام میں الجھاؤ ہے بدائع کی عبارت بالکل واضح ہے۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah volume 13. If it goes, the period becomes unknown. Page 221. Book of Musaqat. Explanation: In the first issue, regarding giving the roots of clover (barsim) for protection until the last yield, it was said to be permissible without specifying a period, but here they are calling it fasid. The difference is that in the first case it was given until the completion of the first yield, and its time is known. And here the meaning is: to protect until the growth of its roots ends, rather until the roots dry. So the period of drying and growth is not known; rather as long as it remains in the ground, growth continues and drying may not be realized, so the period is unknown. Therefore without specifying a period this transaction is not permissible. Or if he does not stipulate the condition of ending growth and drying, but gives absolutely until the last yield, then also the same ruling applies: the contract is fasid. However, this proof that was mentioned can only apply to fresh roots (usul ratbah) and not to palm trees (nakheel). For this reason, some commentators said that the author did not mention the proof for palm trees, as the author of 'Inayah said. The mentioned proof can apply to both, and the meaning would be: he gave a date palm tree and said 'protect it, and this contract is between us until this palm dries up', then this contract is fasid because its period is unknown. But if he said absolutely regarding the palm and did not stipulate drying etc., then the contract is valid and will occur on the first fruits as before. However, for clover and garlic, even in the case of absoluteness, there is invalidity because here the termination is not known. Note: The distinction between the first and second cases depends on the knowledge or ignorance of the termination. There the termination is known so it was called permissible; here the termination is not known so it is called fasid. Therefore if he hands over a date palm tree or clover to the worker and does not stipulate the condition 'until its roots go away', and the time of fruiting or the time of the coming of the fruit is known, then this contract is valid. And if the time of the coming of the fruit is not known, then the contract is fasid. (Shami vol.5 p.183) But they made the contract occur upon the first fruit. Also see Majma' al-Anhur vol.2 p.486. Note: 'Allama Kaisi says: 'And if he gives land to plant fresh vegetables, or gives land in which there are established fresh roots and he does not specify the period, then if it is something for which there is no known time for the beginning of its growth or the end of its cutting, the transaction is fasid. And if the time of its cutting is known, it is permissible and will occur on the first cutting, as in the case of a fruit-bearing tree.' (Badai' vol.2 p.186) This statement is completely clear that the basis of permissibility and impermissibility is knowledge or ignorance of the termination. In summary, the statement of the author of Hidayah is not clear; rather there is confusion in the statement. The statement of Badai' is entirely clear.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses the ruling on musaqat (a contract where a worker tends trees in exchange for a share of the fruit) when the period of the contract is not specified with a known end. The text distinguishes between two cases. In the first case, the contract is for a known end (e.g., until the first harvest) and is valid. In the second case, the contract is tied to an uncertain event such as the drying of the roots of clover (barsim) or the complete cessation of growth. Because the time when roots will dry is unknown, the period is considered unknown (majhul), rendering the contract fasid (invalid but not batil). The author then discusses a proof (dalil) that some commentators (like the author of 'Inayah) say applies only to fresh plants (rutabah) and not to date palms (nakheel). However, the majority view is that the proof applies to both, provided the end is known. The passage quotes from Badai' al-Sanai' which clearly states that the permissibility depends on whether the time of cutting (jazz) is known or not. If the time is known, the contract is valid and applies to the first cutting; if not, it is fasid. This is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
مدت معلوم (muddah ma'lumah): A known and specified period of time for the contract.
مدت مجهول (muddah majhulah): An unknown or uncertain period, rendering the contract fasid.
جذة (jazzah): The first cutting or harvesting of the crop or fruit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a musaqat contract fasid when the worker is told to tend the trees until their roots dry?
A) Because the contract lacks a specified share for the worker.
B) Because the time when roots will dry is unknown, making the period majhul.
C) Because drying of roots is an impossible event.
D) Because the contract must be for a fixed number of years.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a musaqat contract hinges on whether the termination period is known (ma'lum) or unknown (majhul); if unknown, the contract is fasid and the worker receives only ujrat al-mithl.

Requirement of Specifying Share as Common (Musha') in Musaqat
Explaining that the share of fruit must be specified as a common fraction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid musaqat contract and apply it to distinguish valid from fasid stipulations.

Core Idea
In musaqat, the worker's share must be a common fraction (musha'); specifying a specific part destroys the partnership and invalidates the contract.

This lesson explains a key condition for the validity of a musaqat (contract for tending fruit trees). The share of the fruit that the worker receives must be specified as a common share (juz' musha') – a fraction or percentage of the total yield, not a specific tree or quantity. This condition ensures that the owner and worker remain partners in the produce, which is the essence of musaqat. Understanding this condition helps you avoid common errors that render the contract fasid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The passage states that it is a condition to specify the part as common (musha'). Identify what 'common share' means in this context.
A common share is an undivided fraction of the total produce, e.g., half or one-third.
2
Compare to muzara'ah
The passage references muzara'ah (sharecropping). Explain the similarity: why the same condition applies.
Both contracts involve partnership in the yield; a specific part would break the partnership.
3
Understand the consequence
If a specific part is stipulated instead of a common share, what happens? State the legal consequence (fasid).
The contract becomes fasid (corrupted) because the partnership is terminated.
4
Grasp the rationale
Why does a specific part destroy the partnership (shirkah)? Explain the underlying logic.
Partnership requires undivided ownership in the common yield; a specific part creates separate ownership.
5
Apply
Given a scenario where the owner says 'you get the fruit of the date palm by the door,' determine the ruling and reason.
This is a specific part, so the condition is fasid and invalidates the contract.

شيوع کے طریقے پر ایک جز کو متعین کرنا شرط ہے
ويشترط تسمية الجزء مشاعـالـمـا بينا في المزارعة الشرط جزء مـعـيـن يـقـطـع الشركة
ترجمہ اور شیوں کے طریقہ پر ایک جزء کو مقرر کرنا شرط ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم مزارعت میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اسلئے کہ معین جزاء کی شرط نہ کت و شتہ کر دی۔ تشریح مزارعت میں گذر چکا ہے کہ پیداوار شیون کے طریقہ پر دونوں میں مشترک ہونا چاہئے یہاں بھی یہی شرط ہے ورنہ اگر ایک کیلئے یہ شرط کر لی جائے کہ پھلوں میں سے ایک کو محل اس کو ملے گا اور باقی دونوں کے درمیان مشترک ہوگا تو یہ شرط فاسد ہے جو عقد کو فاسد کر دے گی کیونکہ شرکت ختم ہوگئی ہے۔
It is a condition to specify a part on the basis of commonality. And it is stipulated to specify the part as common, as we explained in muzara'ah. The condition of a specific part cuts the partnership. Translation: And it is a condition to fix a part on the basis of commonality, due to the proof which we explained in muzara'ah, because the condition of a specific part destroys [the partnership]. Explanation: In muzara'ah it has passed that the produce must be shared between both on the basis of commonality. Here also this same condition applies. Otherwise, if it is stipulated for one that a specific one of the fruits will go to him and the rest will be shared between both, then this condition is fasid and will make the contract fasid, because the partnership has been terminated.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage states a condition for the validity of a musaqat contract: the share of the fruit that the worker receives must be specified as a common share (musha') – that is, a fraction or percentage of the total produce (e.g., half, one-third), not a specific portion like a particular tree's fruit or a fixed number of fruits. This is the same condition as in muzara'ah (sharecropping). If the parties stipulate that the worker will receive a specific part (e.g., the fruit of a particular tree) and the rest is shared, this condition is fasid and invalidates the contract because it destroys the partnership (shirkah) between the owner and worker. The underlying reason is that the very purpose of musaqat is partnership in the yield, and specifying a specific part negates that partnership.

Key Terms
جزء مشاع (juz' musha'): A common share; an undivided fraction of the total produce (e.g., half, one-third).
شركة (shirkah): Partnership; in musaqat, the owner and worker are partners in the fruit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a musaqat contract, what happens if the parties stipulate that the worker will receive the fruit of one specific tree and the rest will be shared?
A) The contract becomes invalid because the share is not common.
B) The contract is valid because the worker's share is clearly defined.
C) The owner must give the worker the fruit of that tree plus a share of the rest.
D) The contract remains valid but the condition is void.

Key Takeaway
In musaqat, the worker's share must be a common fraction (musha') of the total produce; otherwise, the contract is fasid.

Effect of Time Specification on Musaqat Validity
Stating the rulings for when the specified time will certainly not yield fruit, and when it might.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on musaqat to time specifications, distinguishing between certain fruitlessness, probable delay, and total loss.

Core Idea
In musaqat, the purpose is partnership in fruit; if the specified time cannot achieve it, the contract is fasid.

Musaqat is a contract where a worker tends trees in exchange for a share of the fruit. The parties often specify a time period for the fruit to appear. What happens if the period is too short to produce fruit? What if it is uncertain? This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling based on the purpose (maqsud) of the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of certain fruitlessness
Read the first part: if the parties specify a time in which it is certain no fruit will come (e.g., a winter period for a summer fruit), the contract is fasid because the purpose (partnership in fruit) is impossible.
This is clear: the contract fails from the start.
2
Examine the probable scenario
If the time is such that fruit may come within it but may also be delayed, the contract is initially valid because we are not certain of failure.
Uncertainty does not invalidate.
3
Trace the outcomes after the time
If fruit comes on time, the contract is valid and fruit shared. If fruit comes late, the period was wrong, so contract becomes fasid retrospectively, and the worker gets ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage).
Delayed fruit shows error in estimation.
4
Contrast the case of no fruit at all
If no fruit appears at all, the contract remains valid because we cannot tell if the period was wrong; the loss is total, so neither party owes anything.
The contract is not invalidated by total crop failure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مساقات میں ایسی مدت بیان کی جس میں پھل کا نہ آنا یقینی ہے تو یہ معاملہ فاسد ہے وان سميا في المعاملة وقتا يعلم انه لا يخرج الثمر فيها فسدت المعاملة لفوات المقصود وهو الشركة في الخارج ترجمہ اور اگر ان دونوں نے مساقات میں ایسا وقت مقرر کیا اور معلوم ہے کہ اس مدت میں پھل نہیں نکلے گا تو معاملہ فاسد ہو جائے گا مقصود کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ پھلوں میں شرکت ہے۔ تشریح مساقات کا مقصود پھل میں تو جب اتنی مدت مقرر کی کہ اس میں پھل نہ آنا یقینی ہے تو مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا لہذا عقد فاسد ہوگا۔ محتمل مدت بیان کی تو ابھی فساد کا حکم نہیں لگائیں گے ولو سميا مدة قد يبلغ الثمر فيها وقد يتأخر عنها جازت لانا لانتيقن بقوات المقصود ترجمہ اور اگر ایسی مدت مقر رکی کہ اس میں کبھی پچھل آجاتا ہے اور کبھی اس مدت سے مؤخر ہو جاتا ہے تو مساقات جائز ہے اسلئے کہ ہم مقصود کے فوات کا یقین نہیں کرتے ۔ تشریح اگر اتنی مدت بیان کی کہ اس مدت میں کبھی یہاں آجاتا ہے اور کبھی نہیں آتا تو چونکہ فوات مقصود کا یقین نہیں ہے اسلئے ابھی عقد پر فساد کا حکم جاری نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس کا حکم یہ ہے جو آ رہا ہے۔ اگز مقررہ وقت تک پھل آ گیا تو شرکت کے ساتھ عقد درست ہے اور اگر تاخیر سے پھل آیا تو عامل پر اجرت مثل ہے ثم لو خرج فى الوقت المسمى فهو على الشركة لصحة العقد وان تاخر فللعامل اجر المثل لفساد العقد لانه تبين الخطاء في المدة المسماة فصار كما اذا علم ذالك فى الابتداء بخلاف ما اذا لم يخرج اصلا لان الذهاب بـافة فلا يتبين فساد المدة فبقى العقد صحيحا ولا شئى لكل واحد منهما على صاحبه ترجمہ پھر اگر وقت مقرر میں پھل نکل جائے تو پھل شرکت پر ہیں عقد کے صحیح ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر ( اس مدت میں ) پھلوں کا آنا
In musaqat, if a period is specified in which it is certain that fruit will not come, then this transaction is fasid. And if they both specify in the transaction a time in which it is known that fruit will not come, the transaction is fasid due to the failure of the purpose, which is partnership in the fruit. Translation: And if both of them fix a time in musaqat and it is known that fruit will not appear in that period, then the transaction will become fasid due to the failure of the purpose, which is partnership in the fruit. Explanation: The purpose of musaqat is fruit, so when such a period is fixed in which it is certain that fruit will not come, the purpose will not be achieved, hence the contract is fasid. If a probable period is specified, we will not yet rule it fasid. And if they specify a period in which fruit may sometimes come and sometimes be delayed from it, it is permissible because we are not certain of the failure of the purpose. Translation: And if they fix a period in which sometimes fruit comes and sometimes it is delayed from that period, then musaqat is valid because we are not certain of the failure of the purpose. Explanation: If such a period is specified in which sometimes fruit comes and sometimes not, then since there is no certainty of the failure of the purpose, we will not yet pass the ruling of fasid on the contract; rather its ruling is what follows: if fruit comes within the specified time, the contract is valid on partnership; and if fruit comes late, then the worker is entitled to the equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl). Then, if fruit appears in the specified time, it is on partnership due to the validity of the contract. And if it is delayed, the worker gets the equivalent wage due to the invalidity of the contract, because the error in the specified period becomes evident, so it becomes as if it were known initially. Unlike the case where fruit does not appear at all, because the loss is total, so the invalidity of the period does not become evident, so the contract remains valid and nothing is owed by either to the other. Translation: Then if fruit appears within the specified time, then the fruit are on partnership due to the validity of the contract. And if (the fruit's coming) is delayed, then upon the worker is the equivalent wage due to the invalidity of the contract, because the error in the specified period becomes evident, so it becomes as if it were known at the beginning. Contrary to the case where fruit does not appear at all, because the loss is total, so the invalidity of the period does not become evident, so the contract remains valid and nothing is owed by each of them to the other.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage discusses how the validity of a musaqat contract is affected by the time period specified. It presents three scenarios: (1) If the parties specify a period in which it is certain that no fruit will be produced (e.g., winter for a summer fruit), the contract is fasid from the start because the purpose (shirkah in fruit) is impossible. (2) If they specify a period that is possible but uncertain (the fruit may or may not appear within that time), the contract is initially valid. (3) Then, if fruit actually appears within that time, the contract is effective and the fruit are shared as agreed. If fruit appears after the period ends, it becomes clear that the period was incorrectly estimated, so the contract becomes fasid retrospectively, and the worker is entitled to ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) for his work, not a share. An exception is if no fruit appears at all: then the period's accuracy cannot be determined, so the contract remains valid (since the worker cannot demand a share of nothing, and the owner owes nothing). This ruling is based on the principle that the purpose of musaqat is partnership in fruit, and the contract's validity hinges on the possibility of achieving that purpose.

Key Terms
مقصود (maqsud): The purpose of the contract; in musaqat, it is partnership in the fruit.
اجرت مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The equivalent wage; the market rate for similar work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a musaqat contract with a specified time period that is possible but uncertain, what is the ruling if fruit appears after that period ends?
A) The contract remains valid and the fruit is shared as agreed.
B) The contract becomes fasid and the worker gets nothing.
C) The contract becomes fasid and the worker gets ujrat al-mithl.
D) The contract is void from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a musaqat contract depends on whether the specified time makes the purpose (fruit) possible; certainty of failure invalidates, but uncertainty preserves the contract until the outcome clarifies, with appropriate compensation for delayed fruit.

Specifying the Period in Musaqat and Its Effect on Validity
Explains ruling on period specification in musaqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on specifying a period in musaqat and apply it to scenarios where fruit appears, is delayed, or does not appear due to calamity.

Core Idea
A musaqat contract is valid only if the period allows probable fruit; if fruit appears later, the worker gets fair compensation.

In musaqat, the owner of fruit trees contracts with a worker to tend them in exchange for a share of the produce. A key condition for validity is that the contract must specify a period within which fruit can probably appear. But what happens if no fruit appears within that time? The Hanafi school draws a careful distinction based on whether the failure is due to a miscalculated period or an external calamity. Let's walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the essential condition
The passage first reiterates that in musaqat (like mazar'ah), the produce must be shared proportionally between owner and worker. If a fixed amount is assigned to one party, the condition is fasid and invalidates the contract.
This ensures partnership (shirkah) in the produce, which is the purpose of musaqat.
2
Classify the period specification
Next, determine whether the specified period is certain (too short for fruit to appear), probable (fruit may or may not appear within it), or uncertain due to calamity.
The ruling depends on the nature of the period and the actual outcome.
3
Apply the ruling for a certain short period
If the period is known to be too short for fruit to appear, the contract is fasid from the start because the purpose (partnership in fruit) is impossible.
The worker is still entitled to ujrat al-mithl for work done.
4
Apply the ruling for a probable period
If the period is probable (fruit sometimes appears within it), the contract is initially valid. Then check the outcome: if fruit appears within the period, the contract remains valid and shares are distributed as agreed. If fruit appears after the period, the contract becomes fasid retrospectively, and the worker gets ujrat al-mithl.
The error in the period becomes apparent when fruit is delayed.
5
Handle the calamity exception
If no fruit appears at all due to a natural calamity (afah), the contract remains valid because the period was not proven wrong. Neither party owes anything; the worker loses his labor.
This preserves the validity of the contract when external factors intervene.

ترجمہ اور شیوں کے طریقہ پر ایک جزء کو مقرر کرنا شرط ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم مزارعت میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اسلئے کہ معین جزاء کی شرط نہ کت و شتہ کر دی۔

Translation: And fixing a portion on the basis of sharing is a condition, due to the proof we have mentioned in Mazar'ah, because the condition of a fixed reward would invalidate it. Explanation: It has passed in Mazar'ah that the produce must be shared between both on the basis of shares; here also this is the condition. Otherwise, if it is conditioned for one that a specific portion of the fruits is for him and the rest is shared between both, then this condition is fasid (invalid) and it will invalidate the contract because partnership is eliminated. If in musaqat they specify a period in which it is certain that fruit will not appear, then this transaction is fasid due to loss of the purpose, which is partnership in the produce. Translation: And if both specify a time in the transaction such that it is known that the fruit will not appear in that period, then the transaction becomes fasid due to the loss of the purpose, which is partnership in the fruits. Explanation: The purpose of musaqat is partnership in fruit; so when such a short period is fixed that fruit certainly will not appear, the purpose is not achieved, so the contract is fasid. If a probable period is specified, then the ruling of fasid is not given immediately. And if they specify a period in which fruit sometimes ripens and sometimes is delayed beyond it, it is permissible because we do not have certainty of loss of purpose. Explanation: If such a period is specified that fruit sometimes comes and sometimes does not, since there is no certainty of loss of purpose, the ruling of fasid is not applied yet; rather the ruling is as follows: if fruit appears within the fixed time, the contract is valid with partnership; if fruit is delayed, the worker is entitled to compensation (ujrat al-mithl). Then, if fruit appears within the named time, it is on partnership due to validity of the contract. If it is delayed, the worker gets compensation (ujrat al-mithl) due to invalidity of the contract, because the error in the specified period becomes apparent, so it becomes as if it was known from the beginning. Contrary to the case when fruit does not appear at all, because the non-appearance is due to a calamity, so the invalidity of the period is not manifest, thus the contract remains valid, and nothing is due to either party from the other. Translation: Then if fruit comes out within the appointed time, it is on partnership due to the contract being valid. If it is delayed, the worker gets compensation (ujrat al-mithl) due to invalidity of the contract, because it becomes apparent that there was an error in the specified period, so it becomes as if this non-appearance was known from the beginning. Unlike the case when fruit does not appear at all, because the non-appearance is due to a calamity, so the invalidity of the period is not manifest, so the contract remains valid, and nothing is due to either party from the other.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the condition of specifying a period in the musaqat contract. The author begins by reiterating a condition already established in mazar'ah (sharecropping): the produce must be shared proportionally, not fixed for one party. If a fixed portion is assigned to one party, the contract becomes fasid. Then, the focus shifts to the period. The author states that if the period specified is so short that fruit certainly cannot appear, the contract is fasid because the essential purpose—partnership in fruit—is impossible. Conversely, if the period is such that fruit sometimes appears within it and sometimes later, the contract is valid at the outset, but its ultimate validity depends on actual occurrence. If fruit appears within the named time, the contract is valid and the fruit is shared as agreed. If fruit appears after the period, the contract becomes fasid retrospectively, and the worker is entitled to compensation (ujrat al-mithl) for his labor. An exception is made: if no fruit appears at all due to a natural calamity (afah), the contract remains valid, and neither party owes the other anything. The reasoning is that the non-appearance is not due to an error in the specified period but to an external cause. This careful distinction reflects the Hanafi approach of looking at the actual outcome while preserving the underlying principle of partnership.

Key Terms
مساقاة (musaqat): A contract of sharecropping on trees, where the owner provides trees and the worker tends them in exchange for a share of the fruit.
فاسد (fasid): A contract that is defective from inception, failing to meet a necessary condition for validity, but may become void if not rectified; here, it refers to the contract being invalid due to impossibility of achieving the purpose.
اجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The standard market compensation for the worker's labor, paid when the contract is determined to be fasid after the work has been performed.
آفت (afah): A natural calamity or blight that prevents fruit from appearing, without fault of either party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a musaqat contract, if the specified period is one month and it is known that the fruit will not ripen for six months, what is the ruling?
A) The contract is valid because the period was agreed upon.
B) The contract is fasid because the purpose cannot be achieved within that period.
C) The contract is valid but the worker gets full compensation if fruit does not appear.
D) The contract is suspended until fruit appears.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a musaqat contract hinges on the period allowing probable fruit appearance; if fruit is delayed or absent due to calamity, different consequences apply.

Types of Trees Permissible for Musaqat: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Presents the Hanafi view allowing musaqat in all trees and vegetables, and Shafi'i restriction to date palms and grapes, with rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the permissibility of musaqat in various trees and rebut the Shafi'i restriction using the argument from general need (hajah) and the Khaybar hadith.

Core Idea
Musaqat is permissible on all trees and vegetables because need is general, not limited to dates and grapes.

In this lesson, we examine a classic disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the scope of musaqat (irrigation sharecropping) contracts. The Hanafi school, as recorded by al-Quduri, permits musaqat on all trees, grapevines, vegetables, and even eggplant roots. Imam al-Shafi'i in his new opinion restricts it to date palms and grapevines. We will explore the reasoning behind each position and understand why the Hanafis argue for a broader application.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what al-Quduri lists as permissible for musaqat: date palms, other trees, grapevines, fresh vegetables, and eggplant roots.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Al-Shafi'i in his new opinion restricts musaqat to only grapevines and date palms.
This is the qawl jadid of Imam al-Shafi'i.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues that musaqat's permissibility comes from the Khaybar hadith, which specifically mentions these two.
The hadith is an ahad hadith with zanni thubut.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the permissibility is based on general need (hajah), which applies to all crops, and the Khaybar hadith does not restrict; rather, the people of Khaybar engaged in musaqat on other trees and vegetables too.
Also, the principle of ta'lil requires generalizing the ruling when the illa is general.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Hanafis allow musaqat on olive trees, apple trees, vineyards, and vegetable fields; Shafi'is only on date palms and grapevines.
This difference impacts which contracts are enforceable in each school.

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مساقات جائز ہے کھجور اور دیگر درختوں میں اور انگور میں اور سبزیوں میں اور بینگن کے پودوں میں اور شافعی نے قول جدید میں فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں مگر انگور اور کھجور میں اسلئے کہ مساقات کا جواز حدیث سے ہے حالانکہ حدیث نے ان دونوں کو (نخل اور کرم کو خاص کیا ہے اور وہ خیبر کی حدیث ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو از حاجت کی وجہ سے ہے اور حاجت عام ہے اور خیبر کی حدیث انہیں دونوں کو خاص نہیں کرتی اس لئے کہ اہل خیبر درختوں اور سبزوں میں معاملہ کرتے تھے اور اگر بات ایسی ہی ہو جیسے شافعی نے گمان کیا ہے تو اصل نصوص میں یہ ہے کہ وہ معلول ( بالعلت ) ہوں خصوصا شافعی کی اصل پر۔
تشریح باغات میں کھجور کے ہوں یا کسی اور چیز کا یا انگور ہو نیز سبزیوں میں اور بینگن وغیرہ میں مساقات جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کا قول جدید یہ ہے کہ مساقات صرف انگور اور کھجور میں جائز ہے کیونکہ مساقات کا جواز حدیث سے ثابت ہے اور وہ حدیث خیبر ہے اور اس حدیث نے مساقات کو انگور اور کھجور میں خاص کر دیا لہذا اور چیزوں میں مساقات جائز نہ ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مساقات کا جواز حاجت وضرورت کی وجہ سے ہے اور حاجت جس طرح ان دونوں میں ہے باقی درختوں اور سبزیوں میں بھی ہے۔ نیز امام شافعی کا حدیث خیبر کو انہیں دونوں میں خاص کرنا محل تامل ہے کیونکہ وہ جس طرح ان دونوں میں معاملہ کرتے تھے ایسے ہی دیگر درختوں اور سبزیوں میں بھی کرتے تھے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And musaqat is permissible in date palms, trees, grapevines, fresh vegetables, and roots of eggplants. Al-Shafi'i said in his new opinion: It is not permissible except in grapevines and date palms, because its permissibility is established by a tradition, and that tradition specified these two, and it is the hadith of Khaybar. Our proof is that permissibility is due to need, and need is general, and the Khaybar tradition does not specify them, because its people used to deal in trees and fresh vegetables as well. And if it were as he claimed, then the principle in texts is that they are reasoned (ma'lula), especially according to his own principle. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And musaqat is permissible in date palms, other trees, grapevines, vegetables, and eggplant roots. Al-Shafi'i said in his new opinion: It is not permissible except in grapevines and date palms, because its permissibility comes from a tradition, and that tradition specified them, and it is the hadith of Khaybar. Our proof is that permissibility is due to need, and need is general, and the Khaybar tradition does not specify them, because its people used to deal in trees and vegetables as well. And if it were as he supposed, then the principle in texts is that they are reasoned (ma'lula), especially according to his own principle. Explanation: Musaqat is permissible in gardens whether date palms or other things, or grapevines, also in vegetables and eggplants etc. Imam Shafi'i's new opinion is that musaqat is only permissible in grapevines and date palms because its permissibility is proven by a hadith, and that hadith is the Khaybar hadith, and that hadith specified musaqat to grapevines and date palms, so musaqat is not permissible in other things. Our proof is that permissibility of musaqat is due to need and necessity, and need is present in both these and other trees and vegetables. Also, Shafi'i's specification of the Khaybar hadith to these two alone is questionable, because just as they dealt in these two, so too they dealt in other trees and vegetables.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the types of trees and plants in which musaqat is permissible. The matn, attributed to al-Quduri, states the Hanafi position: musaqat is permissible in date palms, other trees, grapevines, fresh vegetables (ratab), and eggplant roots. Imam al-Shafi'i, in his new opinion (qawl jadid), restricts musaqat to only date palms and grapevines. His reasoning is that the permissibility of musaqat is established by the hadith of Khaybar, which explicitly mentions these two types, thus limiting the contract to them. The Hanafi response has two parts. First, the permissibility of musaqat is based on general need (hajah), which applies to all trees and plants, not just dates and grapes. Second, the Khaybar hadith itself does not specify only these two; the people of Khaybar had orchards that included other trees and vegetables, and they engaged in musaqat on those as well. Furthermore, the Hanafi argue that even if the hadith were limited, the general principle of legal reasoning (ta'lil) requires that the ruling be understood in light of the underlying cause (illah), which is the need for sharecropping. Since need is general, the ruling should be general. The commentary emphasizes that Shafi'i's interpretation is questionable because the historical practice at Khaybar was broader. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that musaqat is valid on all fruit-bearing trees and plants that produce income through cultivation.

Key Terms
النخل (al-nakhl): Date palms, specifically mentioned in the context of trees on which musaqat is permissible.
الكرم (al-karm): Grapevines; in the text, it refers to vines that produce grapes.
الرطاب (al-ratab): Fresh vegetables or greens; in the context of musaqat, it refers to plants that are harvested fresh, like leafy greens.
أصول الباذنجان (usul al-badhinjan): The roots/plants of eggplants; perennial plants that yield over time, included by Hanafis in musaqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only date palms and grapevines
B) Date palms, grapevines, and all fruit trees, but not vegetables
C) All fruit trees, grapevines, vegetables, and plants like eggplants
D) Only grapevines and date palms according to all scholars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits musaqat on all trees and vegetables based on general need, while the Shafi'i new opinion restricts it to date palms and grapevines based on the Khaybar hadith.

Validity of Musaqah Contract When Fruit Fails to Appear
Ruling on fruit appearance in Musaqah contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a Musaqah contract when fruit fails to appear within the fixed period and identify whether the worker is entitled to ujr al-mithl.

Core Idea
In Musaqah, if fruit does not appear within the fixed period, the contract is fasid and the worker gets ujr al-mithl, unless a calamity prevented fruit entirely.

Musaqah is a contract for tending trees in exchange for a share of the fruit. The ruling hinges on whether the fruit appears within the agreed period. When the fruit fails to appear without a calamity, the contract becomes defective (fasid), entitling the worker to a fair wage (ujr al-mithl). This passage clarifies the distinction between contract validity and compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its purpose
Musaqah is a contract where a worker tends trees in exchange for a share of the fruit. The key condition is that fruit must appear within a fixed period.
The contract is similar to sharecropping (muzara'ah) but for trees.
2
Determine the outcome: fruit appears or not
If fruit appears within the fixed period, the contract is valid (sahih) and the fruit is shared as agreed. If fruit does not appear, the contract becomes fasid (corrupt) because the period was insufficient to produce fruit.
The non-appearance indicates the period was defective from the start.
3
Apply the exception: total fruit failure due to calamity
If fruit never appears at all, it suggests a calamity (e.g., natural disaster) rather than a contract defect. In that case, the contract remains valid, and the worker receives no extra wage.
The default assumption shifts: no fruit = contract defect; total failure = calamity.
4
Consequence of fasid contract: worker gets ujr al-mithl
When the contract is fasid but the worker has performed labor, he is entitled to ujr al-mithl (the standard wage for similar work) because the contract failed due to the owner's miscalculation.
This is a Hanafi principle for fasid contracts where work has been done.
5
Summarize the ruling
The validity of the contract depends on the realistic possibility of fruit within the period. Fruit appears → valid. Fruit does not appear (without calamity) → fasid → ujr al-mithl. Total failure due to calamity → valid → no ujr al-mithl.
This distinguishes between a defective condition and an external cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مؤخر ہو جائے تو عامل کیلئے اجر المثل ہے عقد کے فساد کی وجہ سے اسلئے کہ مدت مقررہ میں خطاء ظاہر ہوگئی تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے یہ ( پھلوں کا نہ آنا ) ابتداء میں معلوم ہوتا ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ پھل بالکل نہ نکلے اسلئے کہ پھلوں کا نہ آنا کسی آفت کی وجہ سے ہے تو مدت کا فساد ظاہر نہ ہوا تو عقد باقی رہا۔ در آنحالیکہ صحیح ہے اور کوئی ٹی نہیں ہے ان میں سے کسی ایک کیلئے اپنے ساتھی پر ۔ تشریح جو مدت مقررتھی اگر اس میں پھل آ گیا تو عقد صحیح ہے اور پھل شرط کے مطابق ان دونوں میں مشترک ہوں گے۔ اور اگر پھل نہ آیا تو عقد فاسد ہو گیا اور اب عامل کو اجرت مثلیہ ملے گی کیونکہ اگر شروع ہی سے اتنی مدت مقرر کی جتنی جس میں پھل نہ آنا یقینی ہے تو وہاں عقد فاسد ہوتا ہے تو جب مدت مقررہ میں پھل نہیں آیا تو یہ بھی ایسا ہی ہو گیا کہ اتنی مدت مقرر کی ہے جس میں پھل نہیں آتا لہذا یہ بھی فاسد ہوگی۔ ہاں اگر بالکل ہی پھل نہ آئے تو یہ اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ مدت تو درست ہے مگر کوئی آفت ہے جس کی وجہ سے پھل نہیں آیا تو یہاں عقد صحیح ہو گا اور جب عقد صحیح ہے تو عامل کو کچھ اجر نہ ملے گا۔
If (the fruit) is delayed, then for the worker there is ujr al-mithl (wage of the like) due to the corruption of the contract, because within the fixed period the deficiency became apparent, so it became as if this (non-appearance of fruit) was known from the beginning, contrary to the case when the fruit does not appear at all because the non-appearance of fruit is due to some calamity, so the corruption of the period did not become apparent, so the contract remained while it is valid and there is nothing for any one of them over his partner. Explanation: The fixed period: if fruit appears within it, the contract is valid and the fruit will be shared between them according to the condition. And if fruit does not appear, the contract becomes fasid (corrupt), and now the worker will get ujr al-mithl, because if right from the beginning a period had been fixed in which non-appearance of fruit is certain, then there the contract would be fasid. So when fruit does not appear in the fixed period, it becomes like that: a period was fixed in which fruit does not come, hence it is also fasid. Yes, if fruit does not appear at all, this is a sign that the period is correct but there is some calamity due to which fruit did not appear; here the contract will be valid, and when the contract is valid, the worker will not get any wage.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the Musaqah (contract of tree-tending) when the fruit does not appear within the fixed period. The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) If fruit appears within the fixed period, the contract is valid and the fruit is shared according to the agreed condition. (2) If fruit does not appear, the contract becomes fasid (corrupt), and the worker is entitled to ujr al-mithl (the standard wage for similar work) because the non-appearance indicates that the period was insufficient or defective. However, if fruit never appears at all, that suggests an external calamity (like a natural disaster) rather than a flaw in the contract, so the contract remains valid and the worker receives no wage. The Hanafi position emphasizes the intention and effect of the contract: validity depends on whether the worker's effort can produce fruit within the agreed time. If the period is such that fruit cannot possibly appear, the contract is invalid from the start.

Key Terms
اجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The standard wage for similar work when the contract is fasid and no specific wage was agreed.
عقد فاسد (aqd fasid): A contract that is defective in its conditions but not inherently invalid (batil).
مزارعه (musaqah): A contract of tree-tending in exchange for a share of the fruit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a fixed period is set in a Musaqah contract and fruit does not appear within that period, what is the ruling?
A) The contract is batil and the worker gets nothing.
B) The contract is fasid and the worker gets ujr al-mithl.
C) The contract remains valid and the worker gets nothing.
D) The contract is valid and the worker gets full share.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a Musaqah contract depends on the realistic possibility of fruit appearing within the fixed period; if not, the contract becomes fasid with compensation for the worker, unless a calamity caused total fruit failure.
