Types of Plants for Which Musaqah is Valid: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on Musaqah validity for various plants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which plants Musaqah is valid for, explain the Hanafi proof from general need and the Khaybar hadith, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Musaqah is valid for all plants because its cause—need—is general, not limited to date palms and grapevines.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the scope of Musaqah. While the Shafi'i school restricts the contract to date palms and grapevines based on the Khaybar hadith, the Hanafis extend it to all trees and vegetables using the concept of 'illah (effective cause) and the principle of general need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Al-Quduri explicitly states that Musaqah is valid for date palms, trees, grapevines, vegetables, and eggplant roots. Recognize the broad scope.
The term 'shajar' (trees) here includes fruit trees like apples, pomegranates, etc.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i restriction
Imam al-Shafi'i in his new opinion restricts Musaqah to date palms and grapevines, citing the Khaybar hadith as his proof. Understand that his argument is based on textual specificity.
Al-Shafi'i uses the explicit mention of 'nakhil' and 'karm' in the hadith.
3
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: textual argument
The Hanafi response first argues that the Khaybar hadith does not actually specify, because historical evidence shows the people of Khaybar also dealt with other trees and vegetables. This refutes the claim of exclusivity.
The Hanafi position relies on the broader context of practice.
4
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: qiyasi argument
Even if the hadith were specific, the Hanafi school argues that the ruling is based on a cause ('illah), which is general need (hajah). Since need exists for all plants, the ruling applies universally. This argument is strengthened by noting that Shafi'i's own usul accepts cause-based reasoning.
The principle 'al-hukm yaduru ma'a 'illatihi wujudan wa 'adaman' applies.
5
Understand the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: Hanafis can use Musaqah for any tree or vegetable crop; Shafi'is cannot, and must use alternative contracts like ijarah or muzara'ah for non-restricted plants.
This difference directly impacts agricultural partnerships.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كھجور، درخت، انگور، سبزیوں اور بیگن میں مساقات درست ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء قال وتجوز المساقاة فى النخل والشجر والكرم والرطاب واصول الباذنجان وقال الشافعي في الجديد لا تجوز الا في الكرم والنخل لان جوازها بالاثر وقد خصهما وهو حديث خيبر ولنا ان الجواز للحاجة وقد عمت واثر خيبر لا يخصهما لان اهلها يعلمون فى الاشجار والرطاب ايضا ولو كان كما زعم فالاصل في النصوص ان تكون معلولة سيما على اصله . ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مساقات جائز ہے کھجور اور دیگر درختوں میں اور انگور میں اور سبزیوں میں اور بینگن کے پودوں میں اور شافعی نے قول جدید میں فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں مگر انگور اور کھجور میں اسلئے کہ مساقات کا جواز حدیث سے ہے حالانکہ حدیث نے ان دونوں کو (نخل اور کرم کو خاص کیا ہے اور وہ خیبر کی حدیث ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو از حاجت کی وجہ سے ہے اور حاجت عام ہے اور خیبر کی حدیث انہیں دونوں کو خاص نہیں کرتی اس لئے کہ اہل خیبر درختوں اور سبزوں میں معاملہ کرتے تھے اور اگر بات ایسی ہی ہو جیسے شافعی نے گمان کیا ہے تو اصل نصوص میں یہ ہے کہ وہ معلول ( بالعلت ) ہوں خصوصا شافعی کی اصل پر۔ تشریح باغات میں کھجور کے ہوں یا کسی اور چیز کا یا انگور ہو نیز سبزیوں میں اور بینگن وغیرہ میں مساقات جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کا قول جدید یہ ہے کہ مساقات صرف انگور اور کھجور میں جائز ہے کیونکہ مساقات کا جواز حدیث سے ثابت ہے اور وہ حدیث خیبر ہے اور اس حدیث نے مساقات کو انگور اور کھجور میں خاص کر دیا لہذا اور چیزوں میں مساقات جائز نہ ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مساقات کا جواز حاجت وضرورت کی وجہ سے ہے اور حاجت جس طرح ان دونوں میں ہے باقی درختوں اور سبزیوں میں بھی ہے۔ نیز امام شافعی کا حدیث خیبر کو انہیں دونوں میں خاص کرنا محل تامل ہے کیونکہ وہ جس طرح ان دونوں میں معاملہ کرتے تھے ایسے ہی دیگر درختوں اور سبزیوں میں بھی کرتے تھے۔ اور اگر تسلیم بھی کر لیا جائے کہ ان کا معاملہ انہیں دو میں ہوتا تھا تو پھر سوال ہوگا کہ اس جواز کی علت کیا تھی ؟ کیونکہ نصوص میں اصل یہی ہے کہ وہ معلول ہوتے ہیں خصوصاً امام شافعی کے نزدیک اور جب وہ نص معلوم ہے تو وہ علت حاجت ہی نکلے گی اور حاجت عام ان دونون میں اور ان کے غیر میں۔
Date palms, trees, grapevines, vegetables, and eggplants - is Musaqah valid in them or not? Statements of jurists: He (al-Quduri) said: Musaqah is valid in date palms, trees, grapevines, vegetables, and eggplant roots. Al-Shafi'i said in his new opinion: It is not valid except in grapevines and date palms, because its permissibility is by tradition (athar) and it has specified them both, and that is the hadith of Khaybar. Our proof: Permissibility is due to need, and need is general, and the Khaybar tradition does not specify them both, because its people used to deal in trees and vegetables as well. And if it were as he claimed, the principle regarding texts is that they are subject to cause, especially according to his principle. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Musaqah is valid in date palms and other trees, and in grapevines, and in vegetables, and in eggplant plants. Al-Shafi'i said in his new opinion: It is not valid except in grapevines and date palms, because the permissibility of Musaqah is proven by hadith, and that hadith is the hadith of Khaybar, and that hadith has specified Musaqah for grapevines and date palms only. Therefore it is not valid in other things. Our proof: The permissibility of Musaqah is due to need and necessity, and need, just as it exists in these two, also exists in other trees and vegetables. Also, al-Shafi'i's specification of the Khaybar hadith to these two alone is questionable, because just as they used to deal in these two, they also used to deal in other trees and vegetables. And even if it is conceded that their dealing was only in these two, the question would be: what was the cause (illah) of this permissibility? Because the principle regarding texts is that they are subject to cause, especially according to al-Shafi'i, and when that text is known, then the cause would be need, and need is general in both these and others.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school (represented by al-Quduri) and Imam al-Shafi'i (in his new opinion) regarding the types of plants for which a Musaqah contract is valid. The Hanafi position, stated directly by al-Quduri, is that Musaqah is valid for date palms, other trees, grapevines, vegetables, and even eggplant roots. Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to date palms and grapevines only, based on the hadith of Khaybar, which mentions these two. The Hanafi response argues that permissibility is based on general need (hajah), which is present in all types of plants. Furthermore, the Khaybar hadith does not necessarily restrict the practice to those two, as historical evidence shows that the people of Khaybar also dealt with other trees and vegetables. Even if the hadith is taken as specific, the Hanafi method of istidlal (legal reasoning) emphasizes that the effective cause ('illah) of permissibility is need, and in texts, rulings are understood to be based on causes ('ilal). Since need is general, the ruling applies to all plants. The commentary also notes that Shafi'i's own usul (principles) accept that texts are 'sabab' (cause) oriented, which supports the Hanafi argument.

Key Terms
مساقاة (musaqah): A contract of partnership in which the owner of trees/vines gives them to a worker to tend and water, in exchange for a share of the fruit.
حديث خيبر (hadith Khaybar): The hadith of the Treaty of Khaybar where the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam) allowed the Jews to work the land in exchange for a share of the produce.
علت (illah): The effective cause or rationale behind a legal ruling that allows qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Explicit text from the Quran
B) General need (hajah) and the practice of the people of Khaybar
C) Ijma of the companions
D) A qiyas on sharecropping

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school extends Musaqah to all plants because the effective cause (need) is general, and the Khaybar hadith does not restrict it.

Dismissal of Worker and Validity When Fruit Already Ripe
Rulings on Musaqah contract termination and validity when fruit is pre-existing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the binding nature of a Musaqah contract and identify the conditions under which a Musaqah on existing fruit is valid or invalid according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A Musaqah contract is binding on both parties unless a valid excuse exists; it is invalid if the fruit is already ripe because work cannot affect the produce.

This lesson examines two foundational rulings in Musaqah: the prohibition of unilateral termination without excuse, and the requirement that the worker's labor must have a genuine impact on the produce. The Hanafi school emphasizes that entitlement to a share is based on actual work, not mere possession. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly applying sharecropping contracts in Islamic finance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Musaqah is a contract where a worker tends fruit trees in exchange for a share of the fruit. The first ruling states that neither owner nor worker may terminate the contract without a valid excuse (udhr).
This highlights the binding nature of the contract.
2
Note the exception
The text contrasts Musaqah with muzara'ah (sharecropping), where the seed owner had more flexibility. In Musaqah, the contract is more binding.
Understand the difference between the two contracts.
3
Examine the condition for validity when fruit already exists
If the fruit on the trees is still developing and will increase with the worker's care, the contract is valid. If the fruit has reached full ripeness and no further growth is possible, the contract is invalid.
The worker's share must be in exchange for productive work.
4
Apply the principle
The core principle is that the worker is entitled to a share only due to his work. If work has no effect, the contract becomes fasid (invalid).
This prevents unjust enrichment.
5
Distinguish the two scenarios
Given a scenario with a date palm or crop, determine whether the fruit is still developing or fully ripe. This dictates validity.
Practice with examples: green crop (valid), ready-to-harvest crop (invalid).

Source Text

تو جائز نہیں ہیں اور ایسے ہی اس قیاس پر ہے جبکہ کھیتی دی اور وہ کچی ہے تو جائز ہے اور اگر وہ کاٹنے کے قابل ہوگئی اور پک گئی تو جائز نہیں اس لئے کہ عامل کام کی وجہ سے مستحق ہوتا اور پورا ہونے اور پکنے والا اس کو عامل کے حوالہ کرتا ہے تو جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر پھل پور انہیں ہوا تھا بلکہ عامل کے کام سے ابھی اس میں بڑھوتری ہوئی تو جائز ہے یہی حکم کھیتی کا ہے اگر پھلوں کے پورا ہونے اور پختہ ہونے کے باوجود اس کو جائز کہہ دیا جائے تو عامل کا استحقاق بغیر عمل کے ہو گا حالانکہ یہ مور د شرع کے خلاف ہے۔
And it is not for the owner of the vineyard to dismiss the worker without an excuse, because there is no harm upon him in fulfilling the contract. Similarly, it is not for the worker to abandon work without an excuse, unlike in sharecropping (muzara'ah) with respect to the owner of the seed, as we have mentioned earlier. Translation: It is not the right of the vineyard owner to dismiss the worker without an excuse, because in fulfilling the contract there is no harm upon him. Similarly, it is not the right of the worker to leave work without an excuse, unlike in muzara'ah where there was no compulsion upon the seed owner, as detailed earlier. Explanation: If there is no excuse, the owner should not dismiss the worker, because fulfilling the contract causes no loss to the owner. Likewise, if there is no excuse, the worker should not leave work; however, in muzara'ah, there was no compulsion upon the seed owner, as previously explained. What will be given to the worker and what is he entitled to? He (al-Quduri) said: If he hands over a date palm that has dates as a musaqah, and the dates will increase with work, it is valid. If they have already reached their full (ripeness), it is not valid. Similarly, based on this, if he gives a crop that is still green (bajl), it is valid; if it has become ready for harvest and ripened, it is not valid, because the worker is entitled (to share) due to work, and there is no effect of work after full growth and ripening. If we permitted it, it would be entitlement without work, and the Shari'ah has not come with that. Contrary to the case before that, because the need for work is established. Explanation: The worker gets the fruit of his work, so it is necessary that the worker's work has some effect on the produce. Here, if there is no effect, the contract will be fasid. If fruit has appeared in the garden and has become as big as it would, and now the owner hands it over to the worker, it is not valid. Yes, if the fruit was not complete, but through the worker's work it will still increase, then it is valid. The same ruling applies to crops. If despite the fruit being complete and ripe it is deemed valid, then the worker's entitlement would be without work, and this is against the Shari'ah.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings on Musaqah. The first ruling states that neither the owner of the vineyard/garden nor the worker may unilaterally terminate the Musaqah contract without a valid excuse. This is because fulfilling the contract causes no harm to either party. The exception mentioned is muzara'ah (sharecropping), where the seed owner was not compelled to continue if the contract was not binding in that sense, as previously explained. The second ruling discusses the situation when the Musaqah contract is made for trees that already have fruit. If the fruit is still developing and will increase with the worker's care, the contract is valid. However, if the fruit is already fully grown and ripe (i.e., no further work can increase it), the contract is invalid (la yajuz) because the worker would be entitled to a share without performing any productive work, which contradicts the principle that entitlement in Musaqah is based on labor. The same principle applies to crops: if the crop is still green and growing, the contract is valid; if it is ready for harvest, it is not. The Hanafi position emphasizes that the worker's share must be in exchange for actual work that contributes to the growth or maintenance of the produce.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse recognized by Shari'ah that allows termination of a contract, such as illness or inability to perform.
مزارعة (muzara'ah): Sharecropping contract where landowner provides land and worker provides labor, with seed from either party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a Musaqah contract on a date palm with existing fruit considered valid according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Always valid regardless of the fruit's condition.
B) Valid only if the fruit is already ripe and ready for harvest.
C) Valid if the fruit will still increase with the worker's efforts.
D) Valid only if the fruit is unripe and will decrease with work.

Key Takeaway
In Musaqah, the worker's share is tied to actual productive work; thus, a contract on fully mature produce is invalid.

Invalid Musaqah: Worker Entitled to Equivalent Wage
States ruling for invalid Musaqah contract based on analogy to invalid Ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for an invalid Musaqah contract and explain its basis on analogy to invalid Ijarah using the Hanafi principle of qiyas.

Core Idea
When a Musaqah contract is invalid, the worker still deserves fair wages because it is analogous to a defective hire.

In Hanafi fiqh, contracts can be sahih (valid), fasid (invalid), or batil (void). A fasid contract is defective in its conditions but not void ab initio. This lesson addresses a crucial question: does the worker in a fasid Musaqah contract get anything for his labor? The answer, based on a clear analogy to Ijarah (hire), is yes—he gets the equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl). Understanding this principle protects workers' rights and shows how Hanafi jurists extend rulings via qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage concerns a Musaqah contract that has become fasid (invalid). The ruling is that the worker (āmil) is entitled to ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage).
Ujrat al-mithl is the market rate for similar labor in that time and place.
2
Locate the legal basis (dalil)
The ruling is not directly from Quran or Hadith but derived via qiyas. The source states: 'because it is in the meaning of invalid Ijarah.'
Ijarah (hire) is a well-established contract with clear rulings for its invalid form.
3
Trace the qiyas structure
Asl (original case): Invalid Ijarah where the worker gets ujrat al-mithl. Far' (new case): Invalid Musaqah. Illa (effective cause): Both contracts share the meaning of hiring labor for a share or wage. Hukm: The worker gets ujrat al-mithl.
The illa is being 'in the meaning of Ijarah' (fī maʿnā al-ijārah).
4
Apply the ruling to Muzara'ah
The passage also analogizes to invalid Muzara'ah (sharecropping), showing that the same qiyas extends to similar agricultural contracts.
This demonstrates internal consistency in Hanafi muamalat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا فسدت المساقاه فللعامل اجر مثله لانه في معنى الاجارة الفاسدة وصارت كالمزارعة اذا فسدت ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب مساقات فاسد ہو جائے تو عامل کیلئے اس کے مثل کا اجر ہے اسلئے کہ یہ اجارہ فاسدہ کے معنی میں ہے اور مساقات مزارعت کے مثل ہوگئی جبکہ مزارعت فاسد ہو جائے۔ تشریح جیسے اجارہ فاسد میں اجیر کو اسکی اجرت مثلیہ ملتی ہے اس طرح مساقات فاسدہ میں بھی عامل کو اجرت مثل ملے گی اسلئے کہ ا مساقات اجارہ کے معنی میں ہے اور مزارعت فاسدہ کا بھی یہی حکم ہے۔
He said: When Musaqah becomes invalid, the worker gets his equivalent wage, because it is in the meaning of invalid Ijarah, and it became like Muzara'ah when it becomes invalid. Translation: Quduri said: And when Musaqah becomes invalid, then the worker gets the wage equivalent to his work, because it is in the meaning of invalid Ijarah, and Musaqah becomes like Muzara'ah when Muzara'ah becomes invalid. Explanation: Just as in invalid Ijarah the worker gets his equivalent wage, similarly in invalid Musaqah the worker gets equivalent wage, because Musaqah is in the meaning of Ijarah, and the same ruling applies to invalid Muzara'ah.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for an invalid (fasid) Musaqah contract. The commentator explains that the worker is entitled to ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) because the contract is analogous to an invalid Ijarah (hiring contract). In Hanafi fiqh, a fasid contract is one that is defective in its conditions but not void ab initio; the worker's labor is still compensated. The analogy is drawn to Muzara'ah (sharecropping) as well. The key legal basis (illa) is that Musaqah is in the meaning of Ijarah, so its invalid form follows the same rule.

Key Terms
مساقات (musaqah): A contract where the owner of trees gives them to a worker to tend and irrigate in exchange for a share of the fruit.
اجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The market-rate wage for similar work in that time and place.
اجارہ فاسد (ijarah fasidah): A hiring contract defective in some condition (e.g., unknown duration) but not void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an invalid (fasid) Musaqah contract, what is the worker entitled to?
A) Nothing, because the contract is invalid
B) Ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) based on analogy to Ijarah
C) Half of the fruit as originally agreed
D) Only if the owner agrees to pay

Key Takeaway
In a fasid Musaqah contract, the worker is entitled to ujrat al-mithl by analogy to invalid Ijarah, ensuring fair compensation for labor even when the contract is defective.

Death Invalidates Musaqah by Analogy to Ijarah
Ruling with qiyas proof: Musaqah invalid by death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that Musaqah becomes invalid upon death of either party and explain the qiyas analogy to Ijarah, including the illa (effective cause).

Core Idea
Musaqah ends with death because it is like Ijarah where personal service terminates.

This passage establishes a key rule about the termination of Musaqah. Unlike some contracts that survive death, Musaqah is dissolved because it is considered a type of Ijarah. The proof is by qiyas jali, a clear analogy. We will explore the reasoning and implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and find the exact legal effect of death on a Musaqah contract. State whether the contract continues, is suspended, or becomes invalid.
The ruling is clear: 'Musaqah becomes invalid with death'.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites a specific proof. What is it? Is it a direct text or an analogy?
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to Ijarah, not a direct Quran or hadith.
3
Understand the illa
What is the common feature (illa) between Musaqah and Ijarah that justifies the analogy?
The text says 'because it is in the meaning of Ijarah' (في معنى الاجارة). The illa is that both involve personal service or work.
4
Confirm the implications
Does this ruling apply to both parties' death? Is there any exception?
The ruling applies to both parties. No exceptions are mentioned.

He said: Musaqah becomes invalid with death because it is in the meaning of Ijarah, and we have explained that in Ijarah. Commentary
This passage establishes that Musaqah, like Ijarah, is a contract that is dissolved by the death of either party. The rationale is the same: the contract is based on personal performance and trust, which ends with death. In Hanafi law, this ruling is analogical (qiyas) to Ijarah, as explicitly stated.

Key Terms
باطل (batil): Void; the contract is dissolved and has no legal effect from the point of death.

Musaqah contract becomes void upon death of either party because it is analogous to Ijarah, which also terminates on death.

When Landowner Dies and Fruit Is Unripe: Worker May Continue by Istihsan
Ruling on worker's duty to care for unripe fruit after landowner's death, with istihsan exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the worker's duty to care for unripe fruit after the landowner's death, explain the role of istihsan in preserving the contract, and identify the three options available to the heirs if the worker insists on early harvest.

Core Idea
When the landowner dies with fruit unripe, istihsan allows the worker to continue care to prevent loss, even if heirs object.

This lesson examines a special case in Musaqah: the landowner dies while the fruit is still unripe (busr). Strict qiyas would invalidate the contract upon death, but Hanafi jurisprudence applies istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve the contract and protect the worker from loss. The heirs may object, but the worker may continue until the fruit ripens. The passage also provides three options for the heirs if the worker insists on an early harvest, ensuring no harm befalls them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the default ruling
Recognize the situation: landowner dies, fruit is unripe. Under strict analogy (qiyas), the contract would end with the death of a party. But the Hanafi school uses istihsan to modify this.
The default ruling 'contract void' is set aside by istihsan.
2
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan is applied to prevent harm (darar) to the worker. The worker has already invested effort; abandoning the unripe fruit would cause total loss. The contract is considered 'remaining' for the purpose of care until ripening.
The harm to the worker outweighs the minor inconvenience to heirs.
3
Analyze the heirs' options if the worker chooses to cause loss
If the worker insists on stopping care (or harvesting early) and thus causes loss to the heirs, the passage gives the heirs three choices: divide the unripe fruit as per the contract, pay the worker the value of his share, or spend on ripening and deduct from the worker's share.
These options ensure the heirs are not harmed by the worker's decision.
4
Connect to analogous rulings (Muzara'ah)
The commentator notes this ruling has a parallel in Muzara'ah (sharecropping). Recognize that Hanafi fiqh often links similar contracts through consistent principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان مات رب الارض والخارج بسر فللعامل ان يقوم عليه كما كان يقوم قبل ذالك الى ان يدرك التمر وان كره ذالك ورثة رب الارض استحسانا فيبقى العقد دفعا للضرر عنه ولا ضرر فيه على الاخر ترجمہ. پس اگر زمین والا مر گیا اور پیداوار پھل ) گدر ہیں تو عامل کو چاہئے کہ وہ پھلوں کی پرداخت کرے ( دیکھ بھال کرے) جیسے اس سے پہلے کرتا تھا یہاں تک کہ کھجور پختہ ہو جائے اگر چہ زمین والے کے ورثہ اس کو نا پسند کریں ( یہ حکم) استحسانا ہے تو عقد باقی رہے گا عامل سے ضرر کو دور کرنے کیلئے اور اس میں دوسرے کا کوئی مضر نہیں ہے۔ تشریح زمین والا مر گیا تو عمل برابر پھلوں کی دیکھ بھال رکھے یعنی استحسانا عقد باقی ہے تا کہ فریقین میں سے کسی کا نقصان نہ ہو۔ عامل ضرر کا التزام کرے تو کیا حکم ہے؟ ولو التزم العامل الضرر ويتخير ورثة الآخر بين ان يقتسموا البسر على الشرط وبين ان يعطوه قيمة نصيبه من البسر وبين ان ينفقوا على البسر حتى يبلغ فيرجعوا بذالك في حصة العامل من التمر لانه ليس له الحاق الضرر بهم وقد بينا نظيره في المزارعة.
If the landowner dies and the fruit is unripe (busr), then the worker should care for it as he used to before, until the dates ripen, even if the landowner's heirs dislike that, by istihsan. So the contract remains to repel harm from him, and there is no harm in it for the other. Explanation: When the landowner dies, the worker should continue caring for the fruit, i.e., by istihsan the contract remains to prevent loss to either party. [Then:] If the worker commits to bear the loss, then the heirs of the other have a choice between: dividing the unripe fruit according to the condition, or giving him the value of his share of the unripe fruit, or spending on the unripe fruit until it ripens and then deducting that from the worker's share of the ripe dates, because the worker has no right to cause them harm. We have mentioned its parallel in Muzara'ah.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where the landowner dies while the fruit is still unripe (busr). Normally, death would invalidate the contract, but by istihsan (juristic preference), the worker may continue to care for the fruit until it ripens to prevent loss. This benefit applies even if the heirs object. However, if the worker insists on harvesting early (commits to bear the loss), the heirs have three options: take the fruit unripe as per the contract, pay the worker the value of his share, or spend on ripening and deduct from the worker's share. These options protect the heirs from harm. The commentator notes this is analogous to the ruling in Muzara'ah.

Key Terms
بسر (busr): Unripe dates or fruit that are not yet fully mature.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows a departure from strict analogy (qiyas) to avoid hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because death does not affect the contract

Key Takeaway
Istihsan preserves the Musaqah contract after the landowner's death when the fruit is unripe, allowing the worker to continue care and preventing loss.

When Worker Dies: Heirs May Continue Caring for Fruit
Ruling that the worker's heirs may stand in his place to care for the fruit after his death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding the worker's heirs continuing to care for fruit and explain the underlying talil (legal reasoning) of mutual benefit.

Core Idea
Upon the worker's death, his heirs step into his role for mutual benefit, overriding landowner's objection.

In a fruit tree contract, what happens when the worker dies before the harvest? Does the contract dissolve, leaving the fruit to spoil? The Hanafi school provides a practical ruling: the worker's heirs may step in to care for the fruit, even if the landowner objects. This ruling is based on consideration for both parties' interests. In this lesson, we examine the passage from Al-Hidayah that establishes this rule and the options available if the heirs wish to harvest prematurely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the worker's death and the subsequent care of the fruit by his heirs. The ruling is that the heirs may (are permitted to) continue, even if the landowner objects.
The ruling is mubah (permissible), not wajib.
2
Locate the talil (legal reasoning)
The reason (illah) is that allowing the heirs to continue is beneficial for both parties (al-nazar min al-janibayn). This is a form of istihsan based on maslahah.
The text explicitly states: 'li-anna fīhi al-naẓar min al-jānibayn'.
3
Apply to the scenario of premature harvesting
If the heirs want to harvest unripe, the landowner is given three options to prevent harm. This is a balance between the heirs' right to continue and the landowner's right not to suffer loss.
The three options are: divide unripe, pay value, or spend on ripening.
4
Note the scope of the ruling
This ruling applies to contracts where the worker's task (caring for fruit) can be continued by others. It does not apply to personal service contracts.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولومات العامل فلورثته ان يقوموا عليه وان كره رب الارض لان فيه النظر من الجانبين ترجمہ اور اگر عامل مرجائے تو عامل کے ورثہ کو چاہئے کہ وہ اس کی دیکھ بھال کرتے رہیں اگر چہ زمین والا اس کو نا پسند کرے اسلئے کہ اس میں جانین کیلئے شفقت ہے۔ تشریح عامل کے مرنے کے بعد اس کے ورثہ پھلوں کی دیکھ بھال کریں گے۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں ورثہ عامل اور رب الارض دونوں کا فائدہ ہے۔ فان ارادوا ان يصرموه يسراً كان صاحب الارض بين الخيارات الثلثة التي بياها ترجمہ پس اگر عامل کے ورثہ نے پھلوں کے کچے توڑنے کا ارادہ کیا تو مالک زمین تین خیارات کے درمیان ہو گا جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح اسلئے کہ اگر در شہ عامل کو کچا توڑنے کی اجازت مل جائے تو رب الارض کا نقصان ہے اسلئے کہ وہی تین اختیارات مالک زمین کو ملیں گے جن کا بار باذکر کیا جا چکا ہے۔
If the worker dies, then his heirs should care for it (the fruit), even if the landowner dislikes that, because there is consideration for both sides. Translation: And if the worker dies, the heirs of the worker should continue caring for it, even if the landowner dislikes, because there is kindness for both sides. Explanation: After the worker's death, his heirs will care for the fruit, because there is benefit for both the worker's heirs and the landowner. [Then:] If they intend to harvest it unripe, then the landowner has the three options that we have mentioned. Translation: So if the worker's heirs intend to harvest the fruit unripe, then the landowner has three options which we have explained. Explanation: Because if the worker's heirs are allowed to harvest unripe, there is harm to the landowner, so the landowner gets the same three options mentioned earlier.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage rules that upon the worker's death, his heirs may step in to care for the fruit. This is for the benefit of both parties, even if the landowner objects. However, if the heirs want to harvest the fruit prematurely (unripe), the landowner has the same three options as in the previous case: divide the unripe fruit, pay the value, or spend on ripening and deduct from the heirs' share. This prevents harm to the landowner.

Key Terms
ورثہ (warathah): Heirs of the worker who stand in his place to fulfill the contract obligations.

Key Takeaway
The worker's heirs may step in to care for fruit after his death for mutual benefit, with the landowner's rights protected against premature harvest.

Worker's Heirs and Their Option After Both Parties Die
Ruling on option after both parties' death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when both parties in a musaqat contract die and identify the basis for why the option goes to the worker's heirs.

Core Idea
Worker's heirs succeed to the property right, not to the choice itself.

We now encounter a scenario where both the landowner (rabb al-ard) and the worker (amil) die during the musaqat contract. The question is: who may decide the fate of the fruit? This passage delivers a clear Hanafi rule grounded in the concept of succession (khilafah) in property rights, distinguishing between inheriting the option (khiyar) and inheriting the right to manage the asset.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the musaqat contract is ongoing and both parties have died. The fruit is still on the trees, either unripe or partially ripe.
This triggers a succession issue.
2
Determine who has the option
The text states the worker's heirs have the choice. Contrast this with a possible assumption that the landowner's heirs would decide.
Option is with worker's heirs.
3
Understand the legal basis
The reason given is that they stand in the worker's place (qiyamuhum maqamahu). This is explained as khilafah in a property right (khilafah fi haqq mali) — i.e., they succeed to the worker's right over the fruit, not to the khiyar itself as an inherited attribute.
Crucial distinction: property right vs. personal right.
4
Clarify the scope of the option
The worker's heirs have the same two choices the worker had: leave the fruit on the trees until ripening or harvest it unripe. They cannot do something outside these options.
They stand exactly in the worker's shoes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ماتا جميعا فالخيار لورثة العامل لقيامهم مقامه وهذا خلافة في حق مالى وهو ترك الثمار على الاشجار على وقت الادراك لا ان يكون وارثة في الخيار ترجمہ اور اگر دونوں مر جائیں تو اختیار عامل کے ورثہ کو ہے ان کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہ خلافت مال حق میں ہے اور یہ کہ پھلوں کو درختوں پر پختگی کے وقت تک چھوڑ دینا ہے نہ کہ وہ اختیار میں وارث ہوں۔ تشریح اسلئے کہ عامل کے ورثہ کو وہی اختیار حاصل ہوگا جو عامل کو تھا یعنی پھل پکنے تک درختوں پر رکھ سکتے ہیں یا کچے توڑ سکتے ہیں۔
If both die, then the choice is for the worker's heirs because they stand in his place, and this is a succession in a property right, which is leaving the fruit on the trees until the time of ripening, not that they are heirs in the choice. Translation: And if both die, then the choice is for the worker's heirs due to them standing in his place, and this is a succession in a property right, which is leaving the fruit on the trees until the time of ripening, not that they are heirs in the choice. Explanation: Because the worker's heirs will have the same choice that the worker had: they can leave the fruit on the trees until ripe or harvest it unripe.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This final passage covers the scenario where both the landowner and the worker die during the contract. The ruling is that the worker's heirs have the option (khiyar) to either leave the fruit on the trees until ripening or harvest it early. This is because they succeed the worker in his property right over the fruit, not as heirs of the choice (khiyar) itself. The landowner's heirs do not have this option; the worker's heirs control the disposition.

Key Terms
خلافت (khilafah): Succession in a property right; the heirs take the place of the deceased in handling the fruit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If both the landowner and the worker die, who has the choice to harvest the fruit or leave it to ripen?
A) The landowner's heirs
B) The worker's heirs
C) Both sets of heirs must agree
D) A judge decides

Key Takeaway
Upon death of both parties in musaqat, the worker's heirs succeed to his property right and thus hold the option to determine the fruit's fate.

Invalid Partnership in Land and Trees: The Qiyas to Qafiz al-Tahan
Ruling on invalid partnership in land and trees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on a contract for planting trees with conditional partnership in land, and explain the analogy to qafiz al-tahan.

Core Idea
A contract stipulating partnership in pre-existing property (land) is invalid because it resembles the prohibited qafiz al-tahan.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, Al-Marghinani addresses a specific contract: a landowner gives empty land to a planter to plant trees, with the condition that the land and trees will be shared equally. Can such a contract be valid? The Hanafi ruling declares it invalid, and the proof is based on a powerful analogy to a prohibited transaction known as qafiz al-tahan. Understanding this ruling helps us grasp the boundaries of valid partnerships and hiring contracts in Islamic commercial law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State what contract is being examined and the legal ruling (hukm level) according to the Hanafi school.
The contract is a conditional partnership in land and trees; the ruling is fasid (invalid).
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
Identify the evidence the author uses: analogy (qiyas) to qafiz al-tahan, which is prohibited by nas (textual evidence).
Qafiz al-tahan is a contract where a miller is hired for a portion of the flour produced.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
Explain how the analogy works: both contracts involve hiring (ijarah) where the wage is a share of the thing produced, leading to uncertainty (gharar).
The asl (original case) is qafiz al-tahan; the far' (new case) is the tree planting contract.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify that there is an alternative proof based on jahalah (ignorance) of the wage, but the author prefers the analogy.
Al-Marghinani states that the analogy-based proof is 'asahhuhuma' (the more correct of the two).
5
Determine the practical consequence (compensation)
State the compensation: all fruit and trees go to the landowner; the planter receives the value of the trees and a fair wage (ujr al-mithl).
The trees cannot be removed due to attachment, so monetary compensation is given.

و من دفع ارضا بيضاء الى رجل سنين معلومة يغرس فيها شجر اعلى ان تكون الارض والشجر بين رب الأرض والغارس نصفين لم يجز ذالك لاشتراط الشركة فيما كان حاصلا قبل الشركة لا بعمله وجميع الثمر والغرس لرب الارض وللغارس قيمة غرسه وأجر مثله فيما عمل لانه في معنى قفيز الطحان اذهو استيجار ببعض ما يخرج من عمله وهو نصف البستان فيفسد وتعذر رد الغراس لا تصالها بالارض فيجب قیمتها واجر مثله لانه لا يدخل في قيمة الغراس لتقومها بنفسها وفى تخريجها طريق اخر بيناه في كفاية المنتهى وهذا اصحهما والله اعلم .
ترجمہ اور جس نے خالی زمین دے دی کسی شخص کو چند معلوم سالوں کیلئے کہ وہ اس میں پودے لگائے اس شرط پر کہ ہوگی زمین اور درخت رب الارض اور فارس کے درمیان آدھے آدھے تو یہ جائز نہیں شرکت کے مشروط ہونے کی وجہ سے اس چیز میں جو شرکت سے پہلے حاصل ہے نہ کہ عامل کے عمل سے اور تمام پھل اور پودے زمین والے کے ہوں گے اور پودے لگانے والے کو اس کے پودے کی قیمت اور اس کے مثل کا اجر ملے گا اس کام کا جو اس نے کیا اس لئے کہ یہ قفیز الطحان کے معنی میں ہے اسلئے کہ یہ اجارہ پر لینا ہے بعض اس چیز کے بدلے جو اس کے عمل سے ہوگا اور وہ باغ کا نصف ہے تو عقد فاسد ہو جائے گا اور پودوں کو واپس کرنا مستعد رہے ان کے زمین کے ساتھ متصل ہونے کی وجہ سے تو ان کی قیمت کو واپس کرنا ضروری ہے اور اس کے مثل کی اجرت اسلئے کہ اجر مثل پودوں کی قیمت میں داخل نہ ہوگا پودوں کے بذات خود قیمتی ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اس مسئلہ کی تخریج میں دوسرا طریقہ ہے جس کو ہم نے کفایتہ انتہی میں بیان کیا ہے اور میدان دونوں میں زیادہ صحیح ہے ۔ واللہ اعلم تشریح شرکت کا مقصد یہ ہوتا ہے کہ جو چیز ابھی حاصل نہیں ہے اس کو حاصل کیا جائے او پہلے سے حاصل شدہ چیز کیلئے شرکت نہیں ہوا کرتی اور کہیں ایسی صورت سامنے آ جائے تو عقد کو فاسد کہا جائے گا۔
ما قبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ تفیز الطحان نا جائز ہے جس کا ثبوت نص سے ہے تو وہ چیز جو فیز لاطحان کے درجہ میں آئے گی اس کو بھی فاسد کہا جائے گا جب یہ تفصیلات ذہن نشین ہو گئیں تو اب سنئے کہ مالک زمین نے ایک شخص کو چند معلوم سالوں کے لئے اپنی زمین دے دی کہ دوسرا اس میں درخت لگائے پھر زمین اور درخت صاحب ارض اور عامل (غارس) کے درمیان آدھے آدھے ہو جائیں گے تو یہ صورت جائز نہیں ہے کیوں؟ اسلئے کہ اس چیز میں دلیل اور بھی ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام عقد مذکور فاسد ہے جس کی دلیل یہ بیان کی گئی ہے کہ عقد قفیز الطحان کے درجہ میں ہے اس وجہ سے فاسد ہے۔ اور شیخ نے کفایت انتہی میں اس کی دوسری دلیل بیان کی ہے جس کا حاصل اجرت کی جہالت ہے اور اس جہالت کی وجہ سے عقد فاسد ہے۔ یعنی رب الارض نے نصف زمین کے بدلے وہ آدھے پودے عامل سے خریدے جو وہ لگائے گا اور شن مجہول ہے کیونکہ پودے ابھی معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے مجبول ہیں اسلئے عقد فاسد ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فر ما تے ہیں کہ ان دونوں دلیلوں میں یہ دلیل پختہ ہے جو ہدایہ میں مذکور ہے۔ عنایہ وغیرہ میں جس کی تفصیل موجود ہے اور نتائج الافکار میں اس پر اعتراض کیا گیا ہے۔ ملاحظہ ہو تا ج ص ۵۰ ج ۸ ۔
And whoever gives empty land to a man for known years to plant trees in it on condition that the land and trees are between the landowner and the planter half and half, that is not permissible due to stipulating partnership in what existed before the partnership, not by his work. And all the fruit and trees belong to the landowner, and the planter has the value of his trees and his fair wage for the work he did, because it is in the meaning of qafiz al-tahan, as it is hiring for some of what comes out of his work, which is half the garden, so it becomes invalid. And the return of the trees is prevented due to their attachment to the land, so their value must be paid and his fair wage, because the wage does not enter into the value of the trees due to their being valuable by themselves. And there is another way of deriving it, which we explained in Kifayat al-Muntaha, and this is the more correct of the two. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific contract in the chapter of Musaqah (irrigation contract). The ruling states: if a landowner gives empty land to a person for a fixed number of years to plant trees, with the condition that the land and trees become shared equally between them, the contract is invalid (fasid). The reason given is that the contract stipulates partnership in the land, which already exists before any work by the planter, so it is not a valid partnership in future produce. Moreover, it resembles qafiz al-tahan—a prohibited form of sharecropping where a miller is hired for a portion of the flour produced. Here, the landowner is effectively hiring the planter in exchange for half the garden produce, which is uncertain at the time of contract. Because the contract is invalid, the planter cannot claim ownership of the trees. Instead, all trees and fruit belong to the landowner. The planter receives compensation: the value of the trees he planted (qimah) and a fair wage (ujr al-mithl) for his labor. The trees cannot be removed because they are attached to the land, so compensation is monetary. The fair wage is separate from the value of the trees because the trees are valuable in themselves, while the wage covers the labor. The author notes that there is another way of deriving the invalidity, based on ignorance (jahalah) of the wage, mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha, but the reasoning based on qafiz al-tahan is considered more correct. The text concludes with a reference to other works for further detail.

Key Terms
مساقاة (musāqāh): An irrigation contract where one party provides land and trees, and the other tends them for a share of the fruit.
قفیز الطحان (qafīz al-ṭaḥḥān): A prohibited contract where a miller is hired for a specific measure of flour (the miller's qafiz), considered a form of gharar.
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The fair market wage for the work performed, not predetermined by the invalid contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the contract of giving empty land to plant trees with condition of half partnership invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the planter did not work
B) Because it resembles qafiz al-tahan, which is prohibited
C) Because the land is not owned by the planter
D) Because the trees might not grow

Key Takeaway
A contract that stipulates partnership in pre-existing property (land) is fasid in Hanafi fiqh because it resembles the prohibited qafiz al-tahan transaction.
